كتاب المكاتب/ باب ما يجوز للمكاتب أن يفعله وما لا يجوز
وكتابة عبده والولاء له إن أدى بعد عتقه وإلا لسيده لا التزوج بلا إذن والهبة لغيره يصح أن المفاوضة، ويجوز إقرار المكاتب بالدين والعين والاستيفاء لأنه لا بد للتجار منه. ولو أقر المكاتب على ولده المولود في الكتابة بجناية لم يجز إقراره لأنه إقرار على غيره، فإن مات الولد وترك مالاً كان ذلك لأبيه وأخر إقراره وصار هو الخصم في الجناية لأنه ظهر المقر له في حقه بإقراره، وكذا لو أقر على ولده بدين لم يجز فإن اكتسب الولد مالاً وأخذه الأب نفذ إقراره عليه في المال مكاتب أو مأذون في يده أمة ادعى رجل أنها أم ولده أو مكاتبته فصدقه المكاتب أو المأذون فيه جاز ويدفعها إليه، وكذلك إن كان معها ولد دفعه إليه لأن إقراره بالوديعة اهـ. قال رحمه الله : (وكتابة عبده يعني يملك المكاتب أن يكاتب عبده لأن الكتابة عقد اكتساب للمال فيملكها كما يملك البيع، وقد يكون الكتابة أنفع من البيع إذ البيع يزيل الملك بنفسه والكتابة لا تزيل إلا بعد وصول البدل، فإذا جاز البيع فأولى أن تجوز الكتابة. وقال الشافعي : لا يملك لأن العقد لا يتضمن مثله ولأنه يؤول إلى العتق وليس له يعتق على مال. قلنا : إنما ملكه على أن الكتابة بيع من نفس العبد وإنما لا يملك الإعتاق على مال وتعليق العتق على أداء المال لأن فيه إثبات الحرية مقصودة. وفي الزيادات : رجل مجهول النسب اشترى عبداً فكاتبه فاشترى المكاتب أمة فكاتبها ثم أقر المولى الأعلى المجهول النسب أنه عبد للمكاتب فهي مكاتبة على حالها للمكاتب الأعلى والمكاتب الأعلى للمكاتب الأسفل لأنه يصح إقراره على نفسه بالرق لأن حريته لم تثبته بدليل إلا أنه غير مصدق في حق المكاتب لما فيه من إبطال حق المكاتب فبقي حراً في حق المكاتب مكاتباً للحر لا لعبد مكاتبه وهذا كمجهولة النسب إذا أقرت بالرق لإنسان لم يبطل نكاحها ويؤدي المكاتب الأعلى بدل الكتابة إلى المكاتب الأسفل لأن مجهول النسب لما أقر بالرق لها صار هو وجميع أكسابه مملوكاً لها وبدل الكتابة من جملة أكسابه ومتى صار مجهول النسب عبداً في حق هذا الحكم لا يبرأ المكاتب إلا بالأداء إلى المكاتبة والمكاتبة تؤدي مكاتبتها إلى المكاتب الأعلى. ثم المسألة لا تخلو إما أن يؤديا متعاقباً أو معاً فإن أديا متعاقباً فأيهما أدى أولاً إلى صاحبه عتق ولا يكون ولاؤه لأحد لأن ما عداه إما عبد أو مكاتب وهما ليسا من أهل الولاية، وأيما أدى آخراً عتق وولاؤه للأول لأنه لما صار حراً صار أهلاً للولاء وإن أديا معاً عتقا ولا ولاء لأحدهما على الآخر لأن عتق كل واحد منهما قرن بعتق صاحبه فلا يكون أحدهما أهلاً للولاء حال عتق صاحبه، وإن عجز أحدهما صار مملوكاً للآخر لأنه إن عجز المكاتب صار مملوكاً للمكاتبة لأنه من كسب مجهول النسب، وإن عجزت المكاتبة فقد صارت أمة للمتكاتب والمقر عبدهما فصارا جميعاً للمكاتب، وإن عجزا معاً عتقت المكاتبة وصار المجهول مع المكاتب عبدين لها لأن المكاتب أقر برقبته لمجهول النسب ومجهول النسب أقر برقبته وجميع أكسابه للمكاتبة فقد صار المكاتب مقراً ،برقبته للمكاتب والمكاتبة لما قبلت المكاتبة من المكاتب فقد أقرت برقبتها للمكاتب فقد اجتمع إقرارها وإقرار المكاتب سابق على إقرار مجهول النسب وآخر إلا قرارين ناسبخ لأولهما لأن للآخر رد الأول ولم يوجد الرد للثاني فصح فصار الاعتبار لإقرار مجهول النسب لأنه آخرهما، وهذا كرجل مجهول النسب أقر بأنه مملوك لعبد رجل وأقر مولى العبد وهو مجهول النسب أنه مملوك لهذا المقر فهما جميعاً مملوكان لعبد مجهول النسب أقر بالرق للمكاتبة والمولى للمكاتبة وهو المكاتب أقر للمكاتب بالرق لمجهول النسب صارا مملوكين للمكاتبة ا هـ مختصراً .
قال رحمه الله : ( والولاء له إن أدى بعد عتقه لأن الولاء لمن أعتق وعتيقة المكاتب الأول وهو أهل للولاء عند عتق الثاني وكان ملكه تاماً فيه عند ذلك فثبت له ضرورة. وفي شرح الطحاوي : وإن أديا معاً عتقا وثبت ولاؤهما من المولى. وفي الأصل: وإن عجز الأول ورد في الرق ولم يؤد الثاني مكاتبته بعد بقي الثاني مكاتباً على حاله، ونظيره العبد المأذون له إذا أذن لعبده في التجارة ثم حجر على الأول بقي الثاني يصير مملوكاً للمولى على الحقيقة، فلو أعتقه نفذ عتقه، ولو كان الأول لم يعجز ولكن مات قبل الأداء ولم يؤد الثاني مكاتبته أيضاً فهو على وجهين : إن ترك الأول مالاً كثيراً سوى ما على المكاتب الثاني وبه وفاء ببدل الكتابة وفي هذا الوجه لا تنفسخ كتابته فيؤدي كتابته ويحكم بحريته في آخر جزء من أجزاء حياته وما بقي يكون لورثته الأحرار، وإن لم يكن له وارثه فلمولاه ويؤدي الثاني مكاتبته إلى وارث المكاتب الأول، وإذا أدى وعتق كان ولاؤه لابن المكاتب حيث يرث ورثته المذكور. الثاني إذا مات ولم يترك وفاء سوى ما ترك على المكاتب الثاني وهو لا يخلو من وجهين : إن كان مكاتبة الثاني أقل من مكاتبة الأول ففي هذا الوجه تنفسخ مكاتبة الأول ويكون عبداً ويبقى الثاني مكاتباً للمولى، وإن كان مكاتبة الثاني مثل مكاتبة الأول أو أكثر منه وهذا الوجه لا يخلو إما أن حل مكاتبه الثاني وقت موت الأول فتنفسخ كتابة الأول فيؤدي الثاني إلى المولى ويحكم بحرية الثاني للحال وبحرية الأول في آخر جزء من أجزاء حياته وما بقي من مكاتبة الثاني تكون لورثة المكاتب الأول إن كان له وارث حر ويكون ولاء الثاني للمكاتب الأول لا لمولى المكاتب الأول، وإن حل المكاتب للثاني بعد موت المكاتب الأول إن كان له وارث وإن لم يطلب المولى الفسخ من القاضي حتى حلت فالجواب فيه كالجواب فيما إذا مات الأول وقد حل ما على الثاني، وإن طلب من القاضي الفسخ تفسخ كتابة الأول فظهر قول المؤلف لو قال أو عتقا معاً بأداء مكاتبتهما لكان أولى ليفيد أن الولاء له في الحالتين. وفي نوادر ابن سماعة عن محمد : إذا مات الأول وقد حل ما على الثاني وقد ترك وفاء إلا أنه دين على الناس ولم يخرج الدين حتى أدى الأسفل إلى الأعلى ينظر في الولاء والميراث إلى أدى الكتابة ا هـ . يوم وفي المحيط : فإن مات الأول عن ابن ولم يترك إلا ما على الثاني ومات الثاني وترك ولداً مولوداً في الكتابة يسعى فيما بقي على أبيه ويؤدي إلى المولى من مكاتبة الأول، فإن فضل
Book of the Mukatab / Chapter of what the mukatab may do and what he may not. He may write kitabah for his slave, and the wala' belongs to him if he (the mukatab) pays after his (the slave's) emancipation, otherwise to his master. He may not marry without permission, but gifting to others is valid as in a mutual partnership. It is permissible for the mukatab to acknowledge (iqrar) a debt, a specific item, and to receive payment, because he cannot do without trade. If the mukatab acknowledges a crime on behalf of his child born during the kitabah, his acknowledgment is not valid because it is an acknowledgment on behalf of another. If the child dies and leaves property, that belongs to his father, and his acknowledgment is postponed, and he becomes the opponent in the crime because the beneficiary appeared in his right through his acknowledgment. Similarly, if he acknowledges a debt on behalf of his child, it is not valid. If the child acquires wealth and the father takes it, his acknowledgment against him in the wealth is valid, whether the child is a mukatab or a ma'dhun. If a man claims that a female slave in his possession is his umm walad or his mukatabah, and the mukatab or ma'dhun confirms him, it is valid, and he hands her over to him. Likewise, if she has a child with her, he hands him over to him, because his acknowledgment is like a trust. End. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And his writing kitabah for his slave means that the mukatab has the right to write kitabah for his slave, because kitabah is a contract for acquiring wealth, so he owns it just as he owns sale. Sometimes kitabah is more beneficial than sale, because sale removes ownership by itself, while kitabah only removes it after receipt of the equivalent. So if sale is permitted, then kitabah is even more permitted. Al-Shafi'i said: He does not have that right because the contract does not entail its like, and because it leads to emancipation, and he does not have the right to emancipate for money. We said: He only owns it because kitabah is a sale from the slave himself, and he does not have the right to emancipate for money and to suspend emancipation on payment because that establishes freedom as the intended goal. In al-Ziyadat: A man of unknown lineage bought a slave and wrote kitabah for him; then the mukatab bought a female slave and wrote kitabah for her; then the higher master of unknown lineage acknowledged that he (the mukatab) is a slave of the (lower) mukatab. So she (the female slave) remains as a mukatabah for the higher mukatab, and the higher mukatab is for the lower mukatab, because his acknowledgment of slavery for himself is valid since his freedom was not proven by evidence, except that he is not believed against the (lower) mukatab due to annulling the right of the mukatab. So he remains free in relation to the (lower) mukatab, a mukatab for a free man, not for his slave's slave. This is like a woman of unknown lineage if she acknowledges slavery to a person; her marriage is not invalidated. The higher mukatab pays the kitabah price to the lower mukatab, because when the person of unknown lineage acknowledged slavery to her, he and all his acquisitions become her property, and the kitabah price is among his acquisitions. Whenever the person of unknown lineage becomes a slave in this ruling, the mukatab is not discharged except by payment to the mukatabah, and the mukatabah pays her kitabah to the higher mukatab. Then the issue is either they pay consecutively or together. If they pay consecutively, whichever pays first to the other becomes free, and his wala' does not belong to anyone because the other is either a slave or a mukatab, and they are not eligible for wala'. Whichever pays later becomes free and his wala' belongs to the first because when he became free he became eligible for wala'. If they pay together, both become free and neither has wala' over the other because the emancipation of each coincided with the other's, so neither is eligible for wala' at the moment of the other's emancipation. If one of them becomes incapable, he becomes the property of the other because if the mukatab becomes incapable, he becomes the property of the mukatabah because he is from the acquisition of the person of unknown lineage. If the mukatabah becomes incapable, she becomes a female slave of the mukatab (the other), and the one who acknowledged (the person of unknown lineage) is their slave, so both become the property of the mukatab. If both become incapable together, the mukatabah becomes free and the person of unknown lineage along with the mukatab become two slaves for her because the mukatab acknowledged his own servitude to the person of unknown lineage, and the person of unknown lineage acknowledged his servitude and all his acquisitions to the mukatabah. So the mukatab acknowledged his servitude to the mukatab and the mukatabah, by accepting the kitabah from the mukatab, acknowledged her servitude to the mukatab. Thus her acknowledgment and the mukatab's acknowledgment preceded the acknowledgment of the person of unknown lineage, and the latter abrogates the former because the latter can reject the former, and since no rejection occurred for the latter, it is valid. So the consideration is for the acknowledgment of the person of unknown lineage because it is the later. This is like a man of unknown lineage who acknowledged that he is the property of a man's slave, and the master of the slave (who is of unknown lineage) acknowledged that he is the property of this acknowledger; then both are owned by the slave of unknown lineage. So the person of unknown lineage acknowledged slavery to the mukatabah, and the master (the mukatab) acknowledged to the mukatab (the other) slavery to the person of unknown lineage; they both become owned by the mukatabah. End, summarized.
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And the wala' is for him if he pays after his emancipation, because wala' is for the one who emancipates, and his (the first mukatab's) freed slave (the second) is the first mukatab, and he is eligible for wala' at the time of the second's emancipation, and his ownership was complete in him at that time, so it is established necessarily. In Sharh al-Tahawi: If they both pay together, they become free and their wala' is established from the master. In al-Asl: If the first becomes incapable and returns to slavery, and the second has not yet paid his kitabah, the second remains a mukatab as before. Its analogy is the authorized slave: if he grants permission to his slave for trade and then the first is interdicted, the second remains, becoming the property of the master in reality. If he then emancipates him, his emancipation is effective. If the first did not become incapable but died before payment, and the second has not paid his kitabah either, then there are two aspects: If the first left much wealth apart from what is owed by the second mukatab and it suffices to pay the kitabah price, then in this case his kitabah is not dissolved; he (the first) pays his kitabah and is judged to be free in the last part of his life, and what remains goes to his free heirs. If he has no heir, it goes to his master. The second pays his kitabah to the heir of the first mukatab. When he pays and becomes free, his wala' is for the son of the mukatab, where his mentioned heirs inherit. Second: if he died without leaving sufficiency except what is owed by the second mukatab, this has two aspects: If the second's kitabah is less than the first's kitabah, then in this case the first's kitabah is dissolved and he becomes a slave, and the second remains a mukatab for the master. If the second's kitabah is equal to or greater than the first's kitabah, then this aspect is either the second's kitabah is due at the time of the first's death; then the first's kitabah is dissolved, the second pays to the master, and the second is judged to be free immediately, and the first is judged to be free in the last part of his life, and what remains of the second's kitabah goes to the heirs of the first mukatab if he has a free heir, and the wala' of the second is for the first mukatab, not for the master of the first mukatab. If the second's kitabah is due after the death of the first mukatab, if the first has an heir and the master does not request cancellation from the judge until it becomes due, then the answer is the same as the answer in the case where the first died and what was due from the second had become due. If he requests cancellation from the judge, the first's kitabah is dissolved. So the author's statement becomes clear: if he had said 'or both become free together by payment of their kitabahs' it would have been better to indicate that wala' belongs to him in both cases. In Nawadir Ibn Sami'ah from Muhammad: If the first died and what was due from the second had become due, and he left sufficiency except that it is a debt owed by people and the debt was not collected until the lower paid to the higher, then the wala' and inheritance are considered at the time of payment. End. And in al-Muhit: If the first died leaving a son and nothing except what is owed by the second, and the second died leaving a son born during kitabah, he (the son) strives for what remains on his father and pays to the master from the first's kitabah. Whatever remains...
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is an expansion from the commentary of Kanz al-Daqa'iq by Imam Zayla'i (author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq). It addresses several rulings regarding the mukatab (a slave under a contract of manumission). The matn states that a mukatab may write a kitabah for his own slave, and the wala' (clientage) goes to him if he pays after the slave's emancipation, otherwise to his master. The commentary explains that the mukatab owns the right to write kitabah because kitabah is a contract for acquiring wealth, similar to sale; in fact it is more beneficial because sale transfers ownership immediately while kitabah delays it until payment. The commentator then addresses Imam al-Shafi'i's objection that the mukatab cannot do this because kitabah leads to emancipation and he has no right to emancipate for money. The Hanafi response is that kitabah is essentially a sale from the slave himself, not an emancipation. The commentary then discusses the mukatab's ability to give gifts (ja'iz) and his acknowledgment (iqrar) of debts and property, which is valid due to necessity for trade. However, his acknowledgment on behalf of his child born during kitabah is invalid because it is an acknowledgment on another. A complex scenario involving a person of unknown lineage (majhul al-nasab) is given to illustrate the effect of multiple acknowledgments and kitabah contracts among slaves, showing how the later acknowledgment can abrogate the earlier. The passage then returns to the issue of wala' when both parties pay at different times or simultaneously, and the rulings when one becomes incapable or dies. The commentary draws from various sources including al-Ziyadat, Sharh al-Tahawi, al-Asl, and Nawadir Ibn Sami'ah, showing the depth of Hanafi fiqh in dealing with layered ownership and contractual relations among slaves. The main takeaway is that a mukatab has limited but significant transactional capacity, akin to a free man in trade, but with restrictions regarding marriage (requires permission) and acknowledgment affecting others.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave under kitabah contract.
كتابة (kitabah): Contract of manumission by payment.
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment of a right/liability.
مجهول النسب (majhul al-nasab): Person of unknown lineage, presumed free.
ولاء (wala'): Clientage right after emancipation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the complex scenario from al-Ziyadat, when the majhul al-nasab acknowledges he is a slave of the lower mukatab, why is he not believed against the lower mukatab?
A) Because his acknowledgment is invalid altogether.
B) Because it would annul the rights of the lower mukatab.
C) Because the lower mukatab is a slave and cannot own slaves.
D) Because the acknowledgment was not witnessed.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a later iqrar can abrogate an earlier one if it would otherwise annul rights, and the order of payment in kitabah determines wala' and ownership upon incapacity.

Ruling on Mukatab's Emancipation and Self-Sale: Invalid Due to Incomplete Ownership
Ruling on mukatab's invalid emancipation and self-sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling regarding a mukatab's attempted emancipation of his slave and self-sale, and explain the legal illah based on the requirement of full ownership of the slave's neck.

Core Idea
Emancipation requires full ownership of the slave's neck; the mukatab lacks it, so his emancipation and self-sale are invalid.

A mukatab is a slave who has contracted with his master to purchase his freedom through installments. Although he has limited earning capacity, his ownership rights are incomplete. The Hanafi school rules that a mukatab cannot emancipate his own slave, even if he offers money, because emancipation is an act that demands complete ownership of the slave's raqabah—something the mukatab does not possess. Similarly, selling himself to his slave is equivalent to emancipation and thus equally invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The passage states two actions by the mukatab: (1) emancipating his own slave, and (2) selling himself to that slave. Both are ruled invalid (batil).
Note that the ruling applies even if the emancipation is for monetary consideration ('ala mal).
2
Determine the Legal Basis (Illah)
The reason given is 'because he is not qualified for emancipation since it can only be imagined from one who owns the neck.' The illah is that emancipation requires full ownership of the slave's neck (raqabah), which the mukatab lacks due to the kitabah contract.
Full ownership means the owner has complete disposal rights; the mukatab's ownership is restricted because he is still a slave.
3
Connect to Hanafi Principle
Emancipation is considered an act of worship (qurbah) and not a form of acquisition (iktisab). The mukatab's earning capacity is for acquisition, not for acts of worship requiring complete ownership.
Thus, emancipation is outside the scope of his permitted actions.
4
Apply to Self-Sale
Selling himself to his slave is equivalent to emancipation because it results in his own freedom, which again requires full ownership of his own neck—which he does not have while still a mukatab.
The ruling is consistent: the mukatab cannot initiate any transaction that results in his own freedom without the master's involvement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله تعالى: (واعتاق عبده ولو بمال وبيع نفسه منه) لأنه ليس بأهل رجع للإعتاق لأنه لا يتصور إلا ممن يملك الرقبة فلا ينفذ عتقه ولو على مال لأنه فيه إسقاط الملك عن العبد بمقابلة دين في ذمة المفلس فلا يكون من باب الاكتساب فلا يملكه وبيع العبد من نفسه إعتاق كما بينا فلا يملكه
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And the emancipation of his slave, even for money, and selling himself to him) because he is not qualified to return for emancipation since it can only be imagined from one who owns the neck, so his emancipation is not valid even for money because it involves removing ownership from the slave in exchange for a debt in the debtor's liability, so it is not a form of acquisition, so he does not own it. And selling the slave to himself is emancipation as we explained, so he does not own it.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: the mukatab does not own the right to emancipate his slave, nor to sell himself to his slave. The reasoning (talil) is that emancipation requires full ownership of the slave's neck ('raqabah), which the mukatab does not have because his ownership is incomplete due to the kitabah contract. Even if the emancipation is for a monetary consideration ('ala mal), it is invalid because it would be like selling the slave to himself, which is essentially emancipation, and the mukatab cannot perform emancipation. This follows the Hanafi principle that the mukatab's actions of acquisition (iktisab) are limited; emancipation is not a form of acquisition.

Key Terms
عتاق (itāq): Emancipation of a slave, transferring ownership from master to slave himself.
مكاتب (mukātab): A slave who has entered into a kitabah contract with his master to pay a sum for freedom.
رقبة (raqabah): The 'neck' of a slave, used idiomatically to denote full proprietary ownership over the slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because emancipation requires the master's permission
C) Because the mukatab cannot use money for this purpose
D) Because the slave is also a mukatab

Key Takeaway
A mukatab cannot validly emancipate his slave or sell himself to that slave because emancipation requires full ownership of the slave's neck, which the mukatab lacks.

A Mukatab Buying His Brother: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on inclusion of non-lineal mahrams in a mukatab's kitaba.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether a mukatab includes his brother in the kitaba, explain the proofs of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A mukatab's kitaba includes lineal descendants but not sibling mahrams according to Abu Hanifa — earnings are limited.

This lesson examines an important intra-Hanafi dispute: when a mukatab (a slave under contract of manumission) purchases a close relative like a brother, does that relative automatically become part of the kitaba? The school's authority, Imam Abu Hanifa, and his two leading disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, differed on this question. Understanding their proofs and the final relied-upon position will sharpen your ability to distinguish between categories of mahram relatives and apply the principle of istihsan in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What does Abu Hanifa rule regarding a mukatab buying his brother? According to him, the brother is not included in the kitaba.
The disputed term is 'brother and similar' (أخوه ونحوه).
2
Identify the opposing view
How do the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) differ? They hold that the brother is included.
Their view is based on general obligation of maintaining ties (silah).
3
Follow the Sahibayn's proof
What dalil do they present? They cite several rulings common to all mahrams: manumission, maintenance, non-reversion of gifts, no hand-cutting for theft.
This is a qiyas from complete mahram relationship.
4
Analyse Abu Hanifa's response
How does Abu Hanifa rebut? He argues the mukatab's ownership is limited; his earnings suffice only for lineal descent. Non-lineal mahrams resemble paternal cousins for kitaba by istihsan.
He restricts kitaba to wilad (lineal kinship) because the contract is tied to earning capacity.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical difference: if a mukatab buys his brother, per Abu Hanifa the brother stays a slave; per Sahibayn he becomes part of the kitaba. The text states 'العمل على هذا الوجه أولى', making Abu Hanifa's view mufta bihi.
This tarjih is from later Hanafi authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأب سواء كان مولوداً أو مشتري في الكتابة والمولود مقدم على المشتري فالمولود يظهر حاله في الحياة وبعد الممات كما تقدم، والمشتري في حال الحياة فقط كما تقدم، والأب يحرم بيعه حال حياة ولده ولم يقبل منه البدل بعد موته حالاً ولا مؤجلاً. وإنما قال «تكاتب عليه» ولم يقل صار مكاتباً لأنه لو صار مكاتباً لصار أصلاً ولبقيت الكتابة بعد موت المكاتب الأصلي وليس كذلك، بل إذا مات المكاتب يباع الأب. فإن قيل: ما الفرق بين المشتري في الكتابة الأولاد وبين ما إذا كاتبه على نفسه وولده الصغير فإنه إذا عتق المشتري لم يسقط من البدل شيء، وأما إذا عتق الصغير الذي تكاتب عليه يسقط من البدل ما يخصه؟ أجيب بأن المشتري تبع من كل وجه فلا يعتبر به في أصل البدل لتقرره قبل دخوله في الكتابة بخلاف الصغير فإنه مقصود بالعقد والبدل في مقابلته فسقط ما يخصه منه. وفي الينابيع: لو ملك الأجداد والجدات أو أولاد الأولاد تكاتب عليهم. وفي الخلاصة: ولو اشترى واحداً من أولاده، وإن سفلوا أو واحداً من أجداده وإن علوا تكاتب عليه. قال رحمه الله: (ولو أخاه ونحوه لا) يعني لو اشترى أخاه أو غيره من محارمه لا يكاتب عليه عند الإمام. وقالا: يكاتب عليه لأن وجوب الصلة تشمل القرابة المحرمة للنكاح ولهذا يعتق على الحل كل ذي رحم محرم منه وتجب نفقتهم عليه ولا يرجع فيما وهب لهم ولا يقطع يده إذا سرق منهم إلى غير ذلك الأحكام فكذا هذا الحكم. وللإمام أن للمكاتب كسباً وليس له ملك حقيقة لوجود ما ينافيه وهو الرق، ولهذا لو اشترى أمة ولده لا يفسد نكاحه ويجوز دفع الزكاة إليه ولو وجد كنزاً والكسب يكفي للصلة في الأولاد ألا ترى أن القادر على الكسب يخاطب بنفقة الولد والوالد ولا يكفي في غيرها حتى لا يخاطب الأخ بنفقة أخيه إلا إذا كان موسراً والدخول في الكتابة بطريق الصلة فتختص بقرابة الولاد، ولأن هذه قرابة تشبه بني الأعمام في حق بعض الأحكام كحل الحلية وجريان القصاص من الجانبين وقبول الشهادة ودفع الزكاة إليه، وتشبه الولاد في حق حرمة المناكحة ووجوب النفقة وحرمة الجمع بين اثنين منهن فألحقناها بالولاد في العتق وبني الأعمام في الكتابة توفيراً على الشبهين حظهما والعمل على هذا الوجه أولى من العمل على العكس. وفي الذخيرة لو اشترى العم والعمة فالقياس أن يصيرا مثله في الكتابة وفي الاستحسان لا يكاتب عليهما.
The father, whether born (into slavery) or purchased during the kitaba, and the born one takes precedence over the purchased one: the born one's status is manifested in life and after death as previously mentioned, and the purchased one only in life as previously mentioned. The father's sale is forbidden during the lifetime of his child, and its substitute is not accepted from him after his death, immediately or deferred. He said 'he is included in the kitaba' and did not say 'he becomes a mukatab' because if he became a mukatab he would become a principal and the kitaba would remain after the death of the original mukatab, but it is not so; rather, when the mukatab dies, the father is sold. If it is said: What is the difference between the purchased (slave) among the children and the case where he makes a kitaba on himself and his young child, for when the purchased one is freed nothing of the payment is reduced, but when the young child who was included in the kitaba is freed, what pertains to him is reduced from the payment? The answer: The purchased one is a dependent in every respect, so he is not considered in the original payment because it was established before his entry into the kitaba, unlike the young child who is intended by the contract and the payment is in exchange for him, so what pertains to him is reduced. In al-Yanabi': If he owns grandparents or great-grandparents or children of children, they are included in the kitaba. In al-Khulasa: If he purchases one of his children, even if lower, or one of his grandparents, even if higher, they are included in the kitaba. He said: (And his brother and similar are not) meaning if he purchases his brother or other mahram relatives, it is not included in the kitaba according to Imam (Abu Hanifa). And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is included in the kitaba because the obligation of maintaining ties includes kinship that is forbidden for marriage, and therefore every such relative is manumitted on account of (his) freeing, and their maintenance is obligatory on him, and he does not take back what he gives them, and his hand is not cut off if he steals from them, and other rulings, so likewise this ruling. For Imam (Abu Hanifa), the mukatab has earnings but does not have real ownership due to what contradicts it, namely slavery, and therefore if he purchases a slave woman of his son, his marriage is not voided, and zakat may be given to him, and if he finds treasure, and earnings suffice for maintaining ties with children; do you not see that the one capable of earning is addressed for the maintenance of the child and the father, but it is not sufficient for others so that the brother is not addressed for the maintenance of his brother unless he is well-off, and entering into kitaba is by way of maintaining ties, so it is specific to the kinship of parentage. And because this kinship resembles that of paternal cousins in some rulings such as permissibility of adornment, mutual applicability of retaliation, acceptance of testimony, and giving zakat to him, and it resembles parentage in the prohibition of marriage, obligation of maintenance, and prohibition of marrying two of them together, so we attached it to parentage in manumission and to paternal cousins in kitaba, giving each resemblance its share, and acting on this is better than the opposite. In al-Dhakhira: If he purchases a paternal uncle and maternal aunt, by analogy they become like him in the kitaba, but by istihsan they are not included in the kitaba.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning whether a mukatab (slave under contract of manumission) includes his close relatives—other than direct descendants—in his kitaba. The text begins by distinguishing between a child born to the mukatab's slave and one purchased: the born child's status (freedom if the father dies solvent) is manifest in life and after death, while the purchased child's status only in life. The father of a child already in the kitaba cannot be sold during the child's life, nor can compensation be accepted after death. If the mukatab dies, the father is sold. A question arises: why does freeing a purchased child not reduce the kitaba payment, while freeing a young child included from the start does? The answer is that the purchased child is merely a dependent, so the original payment is unaffected, whereas the young child is a principal in the contract. Then it states that grandparents and great-grandchildren are included, as per al-Yanabi' and al-Khulasa. The core dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that purchasing a brother or other mahram (non-descendant relative) does NOT include them in the kitaba, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) say it does. Their proof: the obligation of maintaining ties (silah) covers all mahram relatives, similar to the rulings of manumission, maintenance, non-reversion of gifts, and non-cutting of hand for theft. Abu Hanifa's proof: the mukatab has earnings (kasb) but not true ownership (milk haqiqah) due to remaining slavery; thus, his earnings suffice for the maintenance of children and parents but not for others like brothers unless wealthy. Since kitaba is a form of maintaining ties, it is restricted to lineal kinship (wilad). Furthermore, non-lineal mahram kinship (like siblings) resembles paternal cousins in some rulings (e.g., permissibility of adornment, retaliation, testimony) but resembles lineal kinship in prohibition of marriage and mutual maintenance. So, for manumission they are attached to lineal kinship, but for kitaba they are attached to paternal cousins, thus not included. The passage ends with a note from al-Dhakhira: by qiyas, uncle and aunt would be included, but by istihsan they are not.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract of manumission (kitaba) with his master, agreeing to pay a sum in installments in exchange for freedom upon completion.
كتابة (kitaba): The contract of manumission between a master and a slave, allowing the slave to purchase his freedom through payments.
محارم (mahārim): Relatives who are permanently forbidden for marriage due to blood relationship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The brother is not included and remains a slave.
C) The brother becomes automatically free.
D) It depends on the master's permission.

Key Takeaway
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, a mukatab's kitaba covers his lineal descendants but not his siblings or other non-lineal mahram relatives.

Ruling on a Mukatab Selling His Umm Walad: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explaining when a mukatab may sell the umm walad he purchased, with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on whether a mukatab may sell his umm walad and explain the reasoning behind Abu Hanifa's view versus the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A mukatab may sell his umm walad only if he purchased her without her child, because his ownership is contingent.

This passage delves into a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: can a mukatab (a slave who has contracted to purchase his freedom) sell the umm walad (mother of his child) that he owns? The ruling hinges on whether the umm walad was purchased together with her child or alone. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rules of sale in the context of incomplete ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the general rule
The matn states: if a mukatab purchases his umm walad 'with him' (i.e., with her child present), her sale is not permissible. Identify the key restriction: the child's presence triggers the prohibition.
The phrase 'with him' (معه) is critical.
2
Recognize the point of disagreement
The text explains that if the mukatab owns the umm walad without the child, there is a dispute: Abu Hanifa permits the sale, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) prohibit it. Pinpoint the exact divergence.
The dispute only arises when the umm walad is purchased alone, not with the child.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's position and dalil
Abu Hanifa argues by qiyas that the sale should be permissible even with the child, but the prohibition is only as a dependency. Without the child, the dependency disappears, so the sale is allowed. His reasoning centers on the incomplete (suspended) nature of the mukatab's ownership.
Key point: A mukatab's earnings are contingent; permanent status cannot be established.
4
Analyze the Sahibayn's position and dalil
The Sahibayn analogize to a free person: once a woman becomes an umm walad, she cannot be sold. They consider the mukatab's ownership sufficiently complete to establish this status, even without the child.
They argue that the umm walad status is independent of the child's presence.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
The practical consequence: according to Abu Hanifa (the relied-upon view), a mukatab may sell an umm walad purchased without her child. According to the Sahibayn, he may not. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's position.
The text presents Abu Hanifa's view as the default, with the Sahibayn's objection noted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله: (ولو اشترى أم ولده معه لم يجز بيعها) يعني لو اشترى زوجته منها لم يجز له بيعها لأن الولد لما دخل في الكتابة امتنع بيعه لما ذكرنا فتتبعه أمه فامتنع بيعها لأنها تبع له ولا تدخل في كتابته حتى لا يعتق بعتقه ولا ينفسخ النكاح لأنه لم يملكها، وكذا المكاتبة إذا اشترت زوجها غير أن لها أن يتبعه كيفما كان لأن الحرية لم تثبت من جهتها على ما بينا. قيد بقوله «معه» لأنه لو ملكها بدون الولد جاز له بيعها عند الإمام. وقالا: ليس له أن يبيعها لأنها أم ولده كالحر إذا اشترى أم ولده وحدها بدونه. وللإمام أن القياس أن يجوز البيع وإن كان معها الولد لأن كسب المكاتب موقوف بين أن يؤدي فيكون للمكاتب وبين يعجز فيكون للمولى فلا يتعلق به ما لا يحتمل الفسخ وهو أمومية الولد إلا أن بيعها امتنع تبعاً للولد وما ثبت تبعاً يثبت بشرائط المتبوع. ولو ثبت بدون الولد لثبت ابتداء والقياس ينفيه، ولا يخفى أن هذا في حال الحياة. وأما في حالة الموت قال في الينابيع: فإذا مات المكاتب وقد اشتراها مع ولدها فلا سعاية عليهما لكن إن أدى ما على المكاتب عند الموت عتقا، وإذا لم يكن معها ولد فقالت أنا أؤدي جميع المال حالاً لم يقبل منها وللمولى بيعها عند الإمام. وفي نوادر بشر عن أبي يوسف مكاتب اشترى امرأته فدخل بها وولدت ولداً بعد الشراء فمات المكاتب عن غير وفاء فالولد يسعى فيما على أبيه. وفي المضمرات وإذا مات الولد في حياة المكاتب ثم مات المكاتب فإن أدت بدل الكتابة حين موته عتقت وإلا ردت في الرق ولا سعاية عليها.
He said: (And if he purchases his umm walad along with him, her sale is not permissible) meaning if he purchases his wife from her, it is not permissible for him to sell her because when the child entered into the kitaba, his sale became prohibited as we mentioned, so his mother follows him, so her sale is prohibited because she is dependent on him and she does not enter into his kitaba such that she would be freed by his manumission nor is the marriage annulled because he did not own her. Similarly, if a female mukatab purchases her husband, except that she may follow him in any case because freedom is not established from her side as we explained. He restricted it with his saying 'with him' because if he owned her without the child, it is permissible for him to sell her according to Imam (Abu Hanifa). And they (the two) said: It is not permissible for him to sell her because she is an umm walad like a free person if he purchases an umm walad alone without him. For Imam (Abu Hanifa), analogy is that the sale is permissible even if the child is with her because the earnings of the mukatab are suspended between his paying and being for the mukatab, and between his failing and being for the master, so it does not attach what cannot be annulled, namely the umm walad status of the child, except that her sale is prohibited as a dependent of the child, and what is established as a dependent is established with the conditions of the followed. If it were established without the child, it would be established from the beginning, and analogy negates it. And this is in life. As for death, he said in al-Yanabi': If the mukatab dies and he had purchased her with her child, there is no sa'yah (earning) on them, but if he pays what was on the mukatab at death, they are free; if he did not have the child with her and she said, 'I will pay all the money immediately,' it is not accepted from her, and the master may sell her according to Imam. In Nawadir Bishr from Abu Yusuf: A mukatab purchased his wife, consummated marriage, and she gave birth to a child after the purchase; then the mukatab died without paying; the child must earn (sa'yah) to pay what his father owed. In al-Mudmarat: If the child dies during the life of the mukatab and then the mukatab dies, if she pays the kitaba payment at his death, she is freed; otherwise she is returned to slavery and no sa'yah is due from her.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a mukatab may sell an umm walad (a slave woman who has borne his child) that he has purchased. The matn states: 'If he purchases his umm walad along with him (i.e., with her child), her sale is not permissible.' The commentary explains: 'with him' means with the child who is already in the kitaba. Since the child is in the kitaba, his sale is prohibited; the mother follows as a dependent, so she also cannot be sold. She does not enter the kitaba herself, so she is not freed by his manumission nor does the marriage (if she was his wife) annul, because he did not own her fully. The same applies if a female mukatab purchases her husband. The restriction 'with him' is key: if he owns her without the child (i.e., she is not an umm walad at the time of purchase), it is permissible to sell her according to Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn say he cannot sell her even without the child because she is an umm walad, just like a free person who purchases an umm walad cannot sell her. Abu Hanifa's reasoning: by qiyas, sale would be permissible even with the child because the mukatab's earnings are contingent—if he pays, it becomes his; if he fails, it belongs to the master—so it cannot establish a permanent status like umm walad for the child. However, the sale is prohibited as a dependent of the child (whose sale is prohibited), and what is established as a dependent requires the conditions of the principal. If it were established without the child, it would be original, but qiyas denies that. After death, if the mukatab dies having purchased her with her child, and he pays at death (i.e., had enough to fulfill the kitaba), both are free; if there is no child, she offers to pay immediately but it is not accepted, and the master may sell her according to Abu Hanifa. From Nawadir Bishr: if the mukatab purchased his wife, consummated, she bore a child, then he died without paying, the child must work to pay the debt. If the child dies before the mukatab, and then the mukatab dies, if she pays at his death, she is freed; otherwise she returns to slavery with no further obligation.

Key Terms
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who has borne a child to her master; upon the master's death, she becomes free, but during his life she has special status.
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract (kitaba) with his master to purchase his freedom by paying installments.
سعاية (sa'yah): Earning or working to pay off a debt or obligation; here, the child's obligation to earn to pay the father's kitaba debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when can a mukatab sell the umm walad he has purchased?
A) He can never sell her.
B) He can sell her only if she was purchased together with her child.
C) He can sell her if she was purchased without her child.
D) He can sell her only after paying off the kitaba.

Key Takeaway
A mukatab's ownership is contingent, so the rules for his umm walad differ from a free person's; the mufta bihi view allows sale of an umm walad purchased without her child.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Immediate 'Aqr for Mukatab Who Purchases and Has Intercourse with a Slave Woman
Explains that 'aqr is due immediately when a mukatab buys a slave woman, has intercourse, and the sale is invalid or the woman reclaimed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that 'aqr is due immediately from a mukatab or ma'dhun who has intercourse with a purchased slave woman that is later reclaimed or the sale invalidated, and explain the legal reasoning based on trade permission.

Core Idea
The mukatab's 'aqr is immediate because purchase is trade, and trade is within his permission.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the liability for 'aqr (compensation for intercourse) when a mukatab (slave in kitabah) or a ma'dhun (slave permitted to trade) buys a slave woman, has intercourse with her, and later the sale proves invalid or the woman is reclaimed by a third party. The author establishes that the 'aqr is due immediately, not deferred, because the transaction falls under the scope of trade permission. Understanding this ruling clarifies the legal boundaries of a slave's authority in commercial dealings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Pinpoint the specific act: a mukatab or ma'dhun buys a slave woman, has intercourse, and then the sale is invalid (fasid) or the woman is reclaimed (istihqaq). The ruling is that 'aqr is wajib immediately.
The act is not the purchase itself but the intercourse under a defective title.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The commentator uses qiyas: the mukatab/ma'dhun is like a wakeel (agent) in trade because both have permission to engage in valid and invalid transactions alike. The liability manifests immediately just as it does for a wakeel.
The proof is aqli (rational analogy).
3
Understand the illa (effective cause)
The illa is that the slave is authorized to trade (idhn fi al-tijarah). Both kitabah and idhn encompass sale and purchase, valid or invalid. Thus any liability arising from such transactions—including 'aqr—is incurred immediately.
Contrast with marriage, which is not trade and where liability is deferred.
4
Distinguish from other scenarios
If the slave had married the woman, 'aqr would not be immediate because marriage is not within the scope of trade permission. This distinction highlights the scope of authorization.
The key differentiator is the nature of the contract: trade vs. non-trade.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإن وطئ أمة بشراء فاستحقت أو بشراء فاسد فردت فالعقر في المكاتبة) كما لو اشترى المكاتب أمة شراء فاسداً فوطئها ثم ردها بحكم الفساد على البائع وجب عليه العقر في الحال، وكذا العبد المأذون له في التجارة لأن هذا من باب التجارة والتصرف تارة يقع صحيحاً وتارة فاسداً والكتابة والإذن ينتظمان البيع والشراء بنوعيهما فكانا مأذونين فيهما كالوكيل بهما فيظهر في حق المولى فيؤاخذ به في الحال
He said (may Allah have mercy on him): ('And if he has intercourse with a slave woman by purchase, then she is reclaimed, or by an invalid purchase and she is returned, then the 'aqr is upon the mukatab.') As if the mukatab bought a slave woman with an invalid purchase, then had intercourse with her, then returned her due to the invalidity to the seller, the 'aqr is binding upon him immediately. Likewise the slave permitted to trade because this is from the chapter of trade, and transactions sometimes occur validly and sometimes invalidly, and the kitabah and permission encompass both types of sale and purchase, so they are permitted in both like the agent, so it manifests against the master and he is held accountable immediately.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling with proof from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The matn states that if a mukatab has intercourse with a slave woman he purchased, and later the sale is found to be invalid (e.g., fasid) or the woman is reclaimed (istihqaq), then the 'aqr (compensation for intercourse) is due from the mukatab immediately. The commentary explains that this applies also to a ma'dhun slave. The reasoning is that purchasing and selling are within the scope of the permission (idhn) granted to the mukatab or ma'dhun. Since they are authorized to engage in trade, including both valid and invalid transactions, any liability arising from such transactions, including 'aqr for intercourse, is effective immediately and binds the master. This is in contrast to marriage, which is not trade and where the liability is deferred.

Key Terms
استحقاق (istiḥqāq): The slave woman is reclaimed by a third party who proves ownership.
عقر ('aqr): Compensation for intercourse with a slave woman, due when the intercourse occurs under a defective title or shubha.
مكاتب (mukātab): A slave who has entered into a kitabah contract to purchase his freedom by paying installments.
مأذون (ma'dhūn): A slave permitted by his master to engage in trade.
وكيل (wakīl): An agent appointed to act on behalf of another in legal matters, including trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does 'aqr become immediately due from a mukatab who has intercourse with a purchased slave woman?
A) Only if the purchase was valid.
B) Only if the purchase was invalid.
C) In both valid and invalid purchases, as long as the woman is reclaimed or the sale is set aside.
D) Only if the master permitted the purchase specifically.

Key Takeaway
The immediacy of 'aqr for a mukatab or ma'dhun hinges on the fact that purchase is a trade transaction within their authorization; any liability from such transactions binds immediately.

Sulh on Deferred Payment in Kitabah: Permissibility by Istihsan
Ruling on sulh in kitabah with istihsan proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school validates a sulh of deferred kitabah payment for immediate half using istihsan, and distinguish it from riba.

Core Idea
In kitabah, the term (ajal) is considered property for the mukatab, so sulh for immediate half is valid by istihsan, balancing the contract.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses a specific case: a master settles with his mukatab for a lesser immediate amount instead of the full deferred sum. While analogy (qiyas) would prohibit this as riba, the Hanafi school applies istihsan to permit it. We will examine the reasoning, including how the term (ajal) is treated as property for the mukatab, and how the sulh can be structured as a rescission and new contract.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and the apparent qiyas
The passage begins with the ruling: if the master settles for half immediately, it is valid. Then it presents the qiyas: exchanging a debt for a term is riba, so it should be invalid. Identify the asl (exchange between free men) and the illa (exchange of debt for non-property).
The qiyas is rejected by istihsan.
2
Understand the istihsan ground
The author gives the istihsan: the term (ajal) is property in one respect for the mukatab because he cannot pay without it. The substitute (badal al-kitabah) is not property in another respect (suretyship not valid). So they balance, avoiding riba. Grasp this dual perspective.
This is a concession based on the mukatab's need.
3
Examine the criticism and defense
A criticism is raised: if borrowing is allowed, why is the term considered property? The defense distinguishes between possible ability (qudra mumkina) and easy ability (qudra maysara). The term provides ease, not mere possibility.
This strengthens the istihsan.
4
Explore additional applications
The passage cites al-Muhit: sulh for a specific object (ayn) is valid; sulh for different descriptions is valid; hiring the mukatab for what he owes is valid and leads to immediate freedom. See how the principle extends.
These show the breadth of the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كاتبه على ألف مؤجلة فصالحه على نصف حال صح والقياس أن لا يجوز لأنه اعتياض عن أجل وهو ليس بمال والدين مال ولهذا لا يجوز مثله بين الحرين ولا في مكاتب الغير وإن لم يجز كان ربا وذلك في عقد المعاوضة غير جائز، وعقد المكاتبة عقد معاوضة لا ينتقض بالمهر والطلاق المقابل وبالمال. وأجيب بأن ذلك على خلاف القياس بالنص، وكذا أن تقول قوله والدين مال منقوض بقوله لو حلف بأنه ليس له مال وله دين على ملى أو معسر لم يحنث إلا أن يقال ذلك في الأيمان فتأمل. ووجه الاستحسان أن الأجل في حق المكاتب مال من وجه لأنه لا يقدر على الأداء إلا به فأعطي له حكم المال وبدل الكتابة من وجه غير مال حتى لا تصح الكفالة به فاعتدلا بخلاف العقد بين الحرين لأنه عقد من وجه فكان رباً، ولأن الصلح أمكن جعله فسخاً للكتابة السابقة وتجديد العقد على خمس مائة حالة . قال بعض الأفاضل في قوله الأجل في حق المكاتب مال : فيه مناقشة ظاهرة إذ قد سبق أن الاستقراض جائز، وبهذا الاعتبار صحت الكتابة حالاً. وأقول : هذه المناقشة إنما تظهر أن لو أرادوا نفي القدرة على الأداء إلا به نفي القدرة الممكنة ما يتمكن به من الأداء، وأما إذا أرادوا بذلك نفي القدرة الميسرة وهو ما يوجب اليسر على الأداء كما هو الظاهر فلا يكون للمناقشة مجال لظهور أن اليسر على الأداء لا يكون إلا بالأجل فتأمل. قال في المحيط : ولو صالحه من الكتابة على عين جاز لأن بدل الكتابة بمنزلة الثمن والاستبدال بالثمن قبل القبض جائز ولا يشترط قبضها في المجلس - كذا في المنتقى عن محمد - لأنهما افترقا عن عين بدين ولو كاتبه على وصف أبيض فصالحه على وصفين أبيضين يداً بيد جاز لأنه صالحه على دين بعين فيجوز ولو استأجر المولى مكاتبه بما عليه سنة بخدمه صحت الإجارة وعتق العبد للحال لأن مولاء ملك بدل الكتابة بالتعجيل فبرئت ذمته عنه، فإن خدمه المكاتب شهراً ثم مات انقضت الإجارة وبرئ المكاتب من صحة ما خدم والباقي دين عليه اهـ .
And if he made a kitabah contract with him for one thousand deferred, then he settled with him for half immediately, it is valid. The analogy is that it is not permissible because it is an exchange for a term, and a term is not property, and a debt is property; therefore, the like is not permissible between two free men, nor in the kitabah of another; and if it is not permissible, it is riba, and that in a commutative contract is not permissible. And the kitabah contract is a commutative contract; it is not invalidated by the dower and the divorce in exchange and by property. And it was answered that that is contrary to analogy by textual evidence. And also you say: his statement 'debt is property' is refuted by his statement: if he swore that he has no property while he has a debt owed by a wealthy person or an insolvent person, he does not break his oath, unless it is said that is in oaths, so reflect. And the ground of istihsan is that the term in the right of the mukatab is property in one respect because he cannot pay except by it, so it was given the ruling of property; and the substitute for kitabah is in one respect not property, such that suretyship for it is not valid, so they balanced. Unlike the contract between two free men, because it is a contract from one respect, so it would be riba. And because the sulh can be made a rescission of the previous kitabah and a renewal of the contract for five hundred in cash. Some virtuous said: in his statement 'the term in the right of the mukatab is property' there is an apparent criticism since it has preceded that borrowing is permissible, and by this consideration the kitabah is valid immediately. And I say: this criticism only appears if they meant by 'cannot pay except by it' the negation of possible ability with which he can pay; but if they meant by that the negation of easy ability, which brings ease in payment, as is apparent, then there is no room for criticism, because it is obvious that ease in payment is only by the term, so reflect. Al-Muhit said: And if he settled with him from the kitabah for a specific thing, it is permissible because the substitute for kitabah is like the price, and exchanging the price before receipt is permissible, and its receipt in the session is not required - as in al-Muntaqa from Muhammad - because they separated from a specific thing for a debt. And if he made kitabah with him for a white description and then settled with him for two white description hand to hand, it is permissible because he settled with him for a debt with a specific thing, so it is permissible. And if the master hired his mukatab for a year in return for what he owes, the hire is valid and the slave becomes free immediately because the master owns the substitute for kitabah by acceleration, so his liability is discharged from it. If the mukatab served him for a month then died, the hire is terminated and the mukatab is free from what he served, and the remaining is a debt on him. End.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the permissibility of a settlement (sulh) in a kitabah contract where the deferred payment is exchanged for a lesser immediate payment. The author (possibly al-Kashghari in al-Muhit) begins by stating the ruling: if a master made a kitabah contract with his slave for a deferred thousand dirhams, then settled (sālahahu) for half of it paid immediately, it is valid. The commentator then presents the qiyas (analogy) that would prohibit it, explaining that exchanging a debt for a term (ajal) is like riba because the term is not considered property (māl) whereas the debt is property; such an exchange between free men is invalid, and so it should be in kitabah. However, the text counters that the kitabah contract is a commutative contract but is not invalidated by such exchanges, as in the cases of mahr (dower) and khul' (divorce in exchange). Then the commentator provides the istihsan (juristic preference) ground: the term, in the context of the mukatab, is considered property from one perspective because the slave cannot pay without it, so it is given the ruling of property; but the substitute for kitabah is not property in another respect (since no suretyship is valid for it), so they balance each other. Thus, the sulh is not riba. Additionally, the sulh can be regarded as a rescission of the original contract and a new contract for the immediate amount. The text then reports a criticism from 'some virtuous' questioning how the term can be considered property if borrowing (istiqrāḍ) is already permissible and the kitabah could have been immediate. The commentator defends the istihsan by distinguishing between possible ability and easy ability (al-qudra al-maysara). Finally, additional rulings from al-Muhit are cited: sulh for a specific object (ʿayn) is valid; sulh for a different description is valid; and hiring the mukatab for what he owes is valid and results in immediate freedom.

Key Terms
الصلح (al-sulh): A settlement or compromise, here changing the terms of the kitabah contract.
الأجل (al-ajal): The deferred term in the kitabah payment, treated as having property-like value for the mukatab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the sulh of a deferred kitabah debt for a lesser immediate amount valid according to istihsan?
A) Because the deferred term is considered money (mal) in the mukatab's case, balancing the contract.
B) Because the master can unilaterally change the terms.
C) Because the slave consented.
D) Because it is a gift, not a sale.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits sulh of deferred kitabah for immediate half by istihsan, reasoning that the term is property for the mukatab.

Burden of Proof in Kitabah Amount Disputes
Furu' rulings on burden of proof in kitabah amount disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who bears the burden of proof when the master and mukatab disagree on the kitabah amount, and explain the consequence if evidence appears later.

Core Idea
In kitabah disputes over amount, the slave's word is taken with oath; master must prove more.

This lesson examines the procedural rules when the master and slave disagree on the terms of the kitabah contract. The Hanafi school gives precedence to the slave's statement due to the principle that the burden of proof lies on the claimant. We will see how this plays out when the master later produces evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
The master claims a higher kitabah amount (e.g., 2000) while the slave claims a lower amount (e.g., 1000).
The dispute can also be about the type of property (e.g., dirhams vs. dinars).
2
Apply the rule of mudda'i and munkir
The master is the claimant (mudda'i) because he claims an extra amount. The slave is the denier (munkir). The burden of proof is on the claimant; the denier takes an oath.
Hanafi principle: al-bayyina 'ala man idda'a wa al-yamin 'ala man ankara.
3
Determine the procedural outcome
The slave's word is accepted with his oath, and the master must provide evidence (bayyina) for his claim.
If the master cannot provide evidence, the slave's statement prevails.
4
Analyze the later evidence scenario
If the judge initially rules based on the slave's word, but the master later brings evidence, the slave must pay the higher amount (if still in kitabah).
The slave works (yas'a) to fulfill the additional amount.
5
Note the istihsan exception
If the slave paid the lower amount, became free, and then the master brings evidence, the slave remains free but owes an additional thousand (istihsan).
This is a juristic preference to balance rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فروع : إذا اختلف المولى والعبد فقال العبد كاتبتني على ألف وقال على ألفين، أو اختلفا في جنس المال القول قول العبد مع يمينه وعلى المولى البينة وإذا جعل القاضي القول قول العبد مع يمينه وألزمه المال وأقام المولى البينة بعد ذلك على ألفين لزمه ألفان ويسعى فيهما، وإن لم يقم البينة فأدى الألف وعتق ثم أقامها بعد ذلك ففي الاستحسان عتق وعليه ألف أخرى. وفي الظهيرية : ولو أقاما البينة فالبينة بينة المولى لأنها تثبت الزيادة لأن المكاتب إذا أدى مقدار ما أقام به البينة يعتق وفي الولوالجية: ولو ادعى كتابة فاسدة والآخر جائزة فالقول قول من يدعي الجائزة والبينة بينة من يدعي الفاسدة، وفي الذخيرة : إذا ادعى المكاتب أنها وقعت فاسدة بأن قال كاتبتني على ألف ورطل خمر وأنكر المولى ذلك القول قول المولى ويلزم المكاتب الكتابة، وكان ينبغي أن لا يقضي بجواز الكتابة بقول الآمر لأن للمكاتب أن نفسه ويفسخ الكتابة ألا ترى إلى ما ذكر في الشهادة إذا قام المولى البينة على العبد أنه يعجز كاتبه بألف وأنكر العبد ذلك فالقاضي لا يقضي ببينة المولى وجواب ما ذكر هنا محمول على الرواية التي تقول إنه ليس للمكاتب أن يعجز نفسه من غير قضاء القاضي.
Branches: If the master and the slave disagree, and the slave says 'You made kitabah with me for one thousand' and the master says 'For two thousand,' or they disagree about the type of property, the word is the word of the slave with his oath, and the master must provide evidence. And if the judge makes the word of the slave with his oath and imposes the amount on him, and thereafter the master brings evidence for two thousand, two thousand are binding on him and he must work for them. And if he did not bring evidence, so he paid the one thousand and became free, then later brought it, then according to istihsan he is free and owes another thousand. And in al-Zahiriyya: If both bring evidence, then the evidence of the master is preferred because it establishes a surplus, because when the mukatab pays the amount for which he brought evidence, he becomes free. And in al-Walwaljiyya: If one claims a void kitabah and the other a valid one, the word is of the one claiming validity, and the evidence is of the one claiming voidness. And in al-Dhakhira: If the mukatab claims that the kitabah occurred void, e.g., 'You made kitabah with me for one thousand and a pint of wine,' and the master denies it, the word is of the master, and the kitabah is binding on the mukatab. And it would be expected that the judge should not rule the validity of the kitabah by the statement of the one saying it (the master?) because the mukatab has the ability to nullify the kitabah himself? Do you not see what is mentioned in testimony: if the master brings evidence against the slave that he is incapable of paying (taʿajjaza) his kitabah for one thousand, and the slave denies it, the judge does not rule based on the master's evidence. And the answer to what is mentioned here is based on the narration that says the mukatab cannot declare himself incapable without a judge's ruling.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage presents a set of subsidiary rulings (furuʿ) concerning disputes between the master and the mukatab over the terms of the kitabah contract. The first ruling: if they differ on the amount (slave says one thousand, master says two thousand) or the type of property (e.g., dirhams vs. dinars), the slave's word is taken with his oath, and the burden of proof is on the master. This is because the slave is the one claiming less, and the principle is that the burden of proof lies on the claimant (al-muddaʿi) and the oath on the denier (al-munkir). The text then discusses a scenario where the judge initially accepts the slave's word, imposes the lower amount, but later the master brings evidence for the higher amount. In that case, the slave must pay the higher amount and work for it (if still in kitabah). If the slave paid the lower amount and became free, and then the master brings evidence, the slave is free but owes an additional thousand (istihsan). Next, if both bring evidence, the master's evidence is preferred because it establishes a surplus (ziyāda). Then, if one claims a valid kitabah and the other a void one, the word is of the one claiming validity, and the burden of proof is on the one claiming voidness. Finally, if the slave claims the kitabah was void due to an invalid condition (like wine), and the master denies, the master's word is taken, and the kitabah is binding. The text notes an apparent inconsistency with the rule that a slave cannot be forced into kitabah, but resolves it by citing a narration that the slave cannot unilaterally declare himself incapable (taʿjīz) without a judge's ruling.

Key Terms
البينة (al-bayyina): Evidence (witnesses) required from the master to prove his claim of higher amount.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): A juristic preference that here allows the slave to be free but still owe the additional amount when evidence appears later.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a slave claims the kitabah was for 1000 dirhams and the master claims 2000, and the judge accepts the slave's word with oath, what happens if the master later brings evidence for 2000?
A) The slave is free and owes nothing more.
B) The slave must pay 2000 and work for it.
C) The slave owes an additional 1000.
D) The slave's original oath is invalidated.

Key Takeaway
In kitabah disputes, the slave's word is credible with oath, but the master can later prove a larger amount, and the slave must pay the difference.

Evidence and Claims of Invalidity in Kitabah
Subsidiary rulings on evidence and validity in kitabah disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules when both parties bring evidence in a kitabah dispute, and when one party claims the kitabah is void.

Core Idea
When both bring evidence, the master's evidence prevails; claims of invalidity shift burden to the one asserting voidness.

This lesson continues with additional furu' from the same passage in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. We examine scenarios where both master and slave produce evidence, and where the validity of the kitabah contract is contested. The Hanafi school applies consistent evidentiary principles to resolve these cases.

Guided Path
1
Both parties bring evidence
If both master and slave present evidence, the master's evidence is preferred because it establishes a surplus (ziyada).
The slave's evidence only proves less; the master's evidence proves more, so it takes precedence.
2
Dispute over validity of kitabah
If one party claims the kitabah is valid and the other claims it is void, the word is of the one claiming validity, and the burden of proof is on the one claiming voidness.
Validity is the default; the one challenging it must prove the defect.
3
Slave claims void due to invalid condition
If the slave claims the kitabah was void because of an invalid condition (e.g., including wine), and the master denies, the master's word is taken and the kitabah is binding.
The slave cannot unilaterally declare the kitabah void; he must have a judge's ruling.
4
Note the exception on ta'ajjiz
The text notes that a slave cannot declare himself incapable (ta'ajjiz) without a judge's ruling, even though he could unilaterally rescind? This is resolved by a narration.
This avoids inconsistency: the slave's power to nullify is limited to certain conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Sick Master's Kitabah: Payment and Rights of Heirs
Intra-Hanafi dispute on kitabah payment deferment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the amount a mukatab must pay immediately when a terminally ill master dies, and identify the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
When a sick master writes kitabah for more than the slave's value, the entire sum is badal al-raqaba; heirs' rights attach to it all, so two-thirds is due immediately.

This passage examines a specific intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf about a mukatab whose terminally ill master died after setting a kitabah sum higher than the slave's market value. The heirs do not consent. The dispute centers on whether the entire kitabah amount is considered the price of the slave's person (badal al-raqaba) or only the value. The answer determines how much the mukatab must pay immediately and how much is deferred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The master is terminally ill, makes kitabah for 2000 to be paid in one year, the slave's value is 1000, the master dies with no other property, and the heirs do not consent.
This specific fact pattern triggers the dispute.
2
State the Position of Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
They hold that the slave must pay two-thirds of the entire 2000 (i.e., 1333.33) immediately and the remainder at the term, or else be returned to slavery.
They consider the entire named sum as badal al-raqaba.
3
State the Position of Imam Muhammad
He holds that the slave must pay two-thirds of the value (i.e., 666.67) immediately and the remainder at the term, or else be returned to slavery.
He analogizes to khul' and argues the excess is a valid deferment from capital.
4
Analyze the Proofs
Sahibayn: the entire amount is badal al-raqaba, so heirs' rights attach to the whole. Muhammad: the master could have set kitabah at value, so the excess deferment is valid like khul'.
The key difference is whether the whole sum is considered a substitute for the slave's person.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf and Mufta Bihi
Practically, the immediate payment differs (1333 vs 667). The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of the Sahibayn, as presented first in the text and generally followed.
The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (مات مريض كاتب عبده على ألفين إلى سنة وقيمته ألف ولم تجز الورثة أدى ثلثي البدل حالاً والباقي إلى أجله أورد رقيقاً يعني المريض إذا كاتب عبده على ألفين إلى سنة وقيمته ألف درهم فمات المولى ولا مال له غيره فإنه يؤدي ثلثي الألفين حالاً والباقي إلى أجله أو يرد رقيقاً، وهذا عند الإمام وأبي يوسف. وقال محمد يؤدي ثلثي الألف حالاً والباقي إلى أجله أو يرد رقيقاً لأن للمولى أن يترك الزيادة بأن يكاتبه على قيمته فكان له أن يؤخر الزيادة وهي ألف درهم بطريق الأولى فصار كما لو خالع المريض امرأته على ألف إلى سنة جاز، وإن لم يكن له مال آخر فصار كله مؤجلاً كما مر في باب الخلع. ولهما أن جميع المسمى بدل الرقبة حتى جرى عليه أحكام الإبدال من الأخذ بالشفعة وغيرها، وحق الورثة متعلق بالمبدل كله فكذا بالبدل بخلاف الخلع لأن البدل فيه لا يقابل المال وإن لم تتعلق الورثة بالمبدل فكذا لا تتعلق بالبلد وحاصله أن المحاباة بالأجل فيعتبر في جميع الثمن وصية من الثالث عندهما، وعنه الأجل فيما زاد على القيمة يصح من رأس المال ويعتبر في قدر القيمة الثلث. قيدنا وقيمته ألف لأنه لو كان بالعكس ففي العتابية : وإن كاتبه على ألف إلى سنة وقيمته ألفان ولم تجز الورثة أدى ثلث القيمة حالاً أورد رقيقاً في قولهم جميعاً لأن المحاباة في القدر وهو إسقاط ألف درهم والتأخير وهو تأجيله الألف فلم يصح تصرفه في ثلثي القيمة لا في الإسقاط ولا في حق التأخير اهـ. وفي المحيط مريض كاتب عبده على قدر قيمته فمات ولا مال غيره يقال عجل لي ثلثي البدل والثلث مؤجلاً كما هو، فإن لم يفعل يرد في الرق. وفيه أيضاً : لو كاتب عبده في الصحة ثم أقر في مرضه باستيفاء بدلها فصدق لأن حق الورثة لم يكن متعلقاً بالعقد فصح إقراره بالاستيفاء كما لو باع أجنبياً في الصحة في ثم أقر باستيفاء الثمن في المرض، ولو كان عليه دين محيط لم يقبل في شيء ويعتق العبد يزعمه ويؤخذ بالكتابة، ولو قال إن مت فكاتبوا هذا العبد تصح الوصية لأنه يملك عتقه فيملك
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (A sick person who made kitabah with his slave for two thousand to be paid in one year, and his value is one thousand, and the heirs did not consent, he pays two-thirds of the substitute immediately and the remainder at its term, or he is returned to slavery) – Meaning: if a sick person made kitabah with his slave for two thousand to be paid in one year, and the slave's value is one thousand dirhams, then the master dies and he has no other property, then he (the slave) must pay two-thirds of the two thousand immediately and the remainder at its term, or he is returned to slavery. And this is according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) and Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said: He pays two-thirds of the one thousand immediately and the remainder at its term, or he is returned to slavery, because the master could have left the excess by making kitabah for his value, so it is more appropriate that he can defer the excess – which is one thousand dirhams – thus it becomes like when a sick man divorces his wife by khul' for one thousand deferred, it is valid, even if he has no other property, then it all becomes deferred as passed in the chapter of khul'. And for them (Imam and Abu Yusuf) the entire named amount is the substitute for the slave (badal al-raqaba) such that the rulings of substitution apply to it, like the right of pre-emption and others. And the right of the heirs attaches to the entire thing substituted (al-mubdal), so similarly to the substitute. Unlike khul' because the substitute in it is not in exchange for property (mal); and since the heirs are not attached to the thing substituted (al-mubdal), they are also not attached to the substitute. The upshot is that the favor (muḥābāh) is by the term; so the entire price is considered a bequest from a third according to them (Imam and Abu Yusuf); and according to him (Muhammad), the term regarding the excess over the value is valid from the capital (ra's al-māl), and regarding the amount of the value, one-third is considered. We specified 'and his value is one thousand' because if it were the opposite, then in al-ʿItābiyya: If he made kitabah with him for one thousand to one year while his value is two thousand, and the heirs do not consent, he pays one-third of the value immediately or is returned to slavery, in all of their sayings, because the favor is in the amount – that is, waiving one thousand – and the deferment – that is, deferring the one thousand – so his disposition is not valid in two-thirds of the value, neither in the waiver nor in the right of deferment. End. And in al-Muhit: A sick person who made kitabah with his slave for the amount of his value, then died and has no other property; it is said: 'Pay me two-thirds of the substitute immediately and one-third deferred as it is; if he does not do so, he is returned to slavery.' And also in it: If he made kitabah with his slave while healthy, then in his illness he acknowledged that he had received its substitute, it is believed (yuṣaddaq) because the right of the heirs was not attached to the contract, so his acknowledgment of receipt is valid – as if he sold to a third party while healthy, then acknowledged receipt of the price in his illness. And if he had an overwhelming debt, it is not accepted at all, and the slave is freed by his claim and is taken for the kitabah. And if he said: 'If I die, then make kitabah with this slave,' the bequest is valid because he owns his manumission, so he owns
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage deals with the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a specific scenario: a master who is terminally ill (mariḍ) makes a kitabah contract with his slave for a sum greater than the slave's value, and then dies. The heirs do not consent to the contract. The ruling concerns how much the slave must pay immediately and what happens if he cannot. According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the entire named amount (alfayn) is considered the price of the slave's person (badal al-raqaba), so the heirs' rights attach to the whole. Since the master's disposition in illness is limited to one-third of his estate, and here the favor (muḥābāh) is in the deferment (ajal), not in the amount, the slave must pay two-thirds of the entire sum immediately (equivalent to the two-thirds of the estate not covered by the bequest) and the remainder at its term; if he cannot, he returns to slavery. Imam Muhammad holds a different view: he analogizes to khul' (divorce in exchange) where the deferred payment is fully valid even if the husband dies. He argues that the master could have set the kitabah at the slave's value (alf), so the excess (alf) is a deferment that is valid from the capital (ra's al-māl) – meaning it does not affect the heirs' rights. Thus, only one-third of the value (thuluth al-alf) must be paid immediately, and the rest deferred. The text then clarifies that this dispute applies only when the slave's value is less than the kitabah amount. In the opposite case (value greater than kitabah amount), all agree that the slave pays one-third of the value immediately because the favor is in the amount (isqāṭ) and the deferment (ta'khīr) combined. Additional rulings from al-Muhit: if the kitabah is exactly for the slave's value, the slave pays two-thirds immediately and one-third deferred. Also, if the master acknowledged receiving the kitabah payment in his illness, it is believed if he was healthy at the time of the contract (since heirs had no right attached). But if the master has overwhelming debt, the acknowledgment is not accepted, and the slave must pay the kitabah. Finally, a bequest to make kitabah for a slave after death is valid.

Key Terms
بدل الرقبة (badal al-raqaba): The substitute or price of the slave's person; here the entire kitabah amount is considered badal al-raqaba according to Imam and Abu Yusuf.
المحاباة (al-muḥābāh): Favor or concession; here it refers to the concession to the slave by deferring payment or waiving part of the amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, why must the mukatab pay two-thirds of the entire kitabah amount immediately when the sick master dies?
A) Because the entire amount is badal al-raqaba and the heirs' rights attach to all of it.
B) Because the master's illness makes the contract void.
C) Because the slave's value is only one thousand.
D) Because the term is considered property.

Key Takeaway
When a sick master sets a kitabah amount higher than the slave's value, the Sahibayn treat the entire sum as badal al-raqaba, making two-thirds payable immediately; Imam Muhammad restricts the immediate payment to two-thirds of the value.
