Mukatab's Option When a Sick Master Frees Him
Ruling on sick master freeing mukatab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a sick master frees his mukatab and explain the option given to the mukatab when the manumission is exactly one-third of the estate and heirs do not approve.

Core Idea
A sick master's freeing of his mukatab is a bequest; if exactly one-third and heirs reject, the mukatab chooses to work for two-thirds of value or two-thirds of kitabah debt.

This passage from Sharh al-Tahawi addresses a specific scenario: a master who is terminally ill frees his mukatab. Islamic law treats such manumission as a bequest, subject to the one-third limit. The passage explains the rules and the option granted to the mukatab when the manumission is exactly one-third and heirs disapprove.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The act is a sick master freeing his mukatab. Sickness triggers the law of bequests (wasiyya). The mukatab is still a slave until the kitabah is fully paid.
The ruling distinguishes between full ownership and co-ownership.
2
Determine the hukm based on the bequest limit
If the manumission is within one-third of the estate, it is effective immediately and the mukatab is free without payment. If it is exactly one-third and the heirs do not approve, a special option arises.
The text only gives these two cases; exceeding one-third is not explicitly covered here.
3
Analyze the option structure
The mukatab may choose to work for two-thirds of his market value or two-thirds of the kitabah debt. This compensates for the partial manumission.
The option is according to Imam Abu Hanifa.
4
Consider the ownership condition
The ruling applies only when the master has full ownership. If the slave is co-owned, the kitabah by one co-owner with permission is valid and heirs cannot revoke it.
This is clarified by the phrase 'his slave' indicating complete ownership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي شرح الطحاوي : من أعتق مكاتبه وهو مريض ينظر ؛ إن كان يخرج من الثلث عتق مجاناً، وإن كان الثلث ولم تجز الورثة ينظر إلى ثلثي قيمته وإلى ثلثي بدل الكتابة وله الخيار يسعى في أيهما شاء عند الإمام وظاهر قوله عبده أن ملكه كامل له وإنما باشر العقد بنفسه ليحترز عما إذا كان بين صحيح ومريض. قال في المحيط : وإن كان العبد بين رجلين مرض أحدهما وكاتبه الصحيح بإذنه جاز وليس للوارث إبطاله، وكذا إذا أذن له في القبض وقبض بدل الكتابة ثم مات المريض لم يكن للوارث أن يأخذ منه شيئاً. وفي الجامع : مكاتب أقر لمولاه في صحته بألف درهم وقد كان المولى كاتبه على ألف وأقر المكاتب في صحته لأجنبي بألف درهم فمرض المكاتب وفي يده ألف فقضاها المولى من المكاتب فمات من ذلك المرض وليس له مال غيرها فالألف تقسم بين المولى والأجنبي على ثلاثة أسهم : سهمان للمولى وسهم للأجنبي. ولو أن المكاتب أدى الألف إلى المولى من الدين الذي أقر به ثم مات فالأجـ أجنبي أحق بهذه الألف وبطل دين المولى ومكاتبته، وإن مات عن غير وفاء فرد في الرق ومات على ملك المولى ويبطل دين المولى وكتابته ولو لم يقبض المولى الألف ومات وتركها فهي للأجنبي. ولو ترك المكاتب ابناً ولد له في الكتابة فالأجنبي أحق بهذه الألف أيضاً المولى ابن المكاتب ويبيع بالدين والمكتابة وإذا أدى الابن الكتابة والدين لا ينقض القضاء للأجنبي. ولو أن رجلاً كاتب عبده على ألف درهم في صحته وأقرضه أجنبي ألف درهم ثم مرض المكاتب وأقرضه درهم بمعاينة الشهود فسرقت من المكاتب وفي يد المكاتب ألف درهم أخرى فقضاها المولى فالمولى أحق بها من الأجنبي بخلاف ما لو اشترى المكاتب في مرضه عبداً . المولى بألف درهم ولرجل أجنبي على المكاتب ألف فهلك العبد وفي يد المكاتب ألف درهم غير فقضاها المولى من ثمن العبد فمات المكاتب من مرضه ذلك ولم يترك وفاء، فما قبض المولى من ثمن العبد لا يسلم للمولى وإن كان البيع وقبض الثمن بمعاينة الشهود فيسترد الألف ويدفع إلى الأجنبي. والفرق أن صورة القرض المماثلة ظاهرة فيقدم المولى ولم تظهر في صورة البيع فقدم الأجنبي فتأمل وفيه أيضاً : كاتب عبده على ألفين وله ابنان حران وهما وارثاه فمرض المكاتب وأقر لأحد الابنين بألف درهم وأقر للمولى بدين ألف فمات وترك ألفي درهم فالمولى أحق بالألفين يستوفي أحدهما من الكتابة والأخرى من الدين، فإن ترك أقل من الألفين يبدأ بدين الابن .اهـ. والفرق هو أنه إذا ترك ألفين أمكن تصوره بعد موته حراً نظراً إلى صورة المؤدي، وإن اختلف بوجه الدفع فقدم المولى لأنه عقد الكتابة على صورة ألفين بخلاف ما إذا ترك الأقل لم يمكن ذلك فقدم الابن فتأمل.
And in Sharh al-Tahawi: Whoever frees his mukatab while sick: if it comes out of one-third, he is free for free; if it is one-third and the heirs do not approve, consideration is given to two-thirds of his value and two-thirds of the kitabah price, and he has the option to work for whichever he wishes according to Imam. And the apparent meaning of his word 'his slave' is that his ownership is complete, and he concluded the contract himself to avoid the case where [the slave] is between a healthy and a sick person. He said in al-Muhit: If the slave is between two men, one of them falls sick, and the healthy one writes a kitabah with his permission, it is valid, and the heir cannot invalidate it. Similarly, if he permitted him to receive and he received the kitabah price, then the sick one died, the heir cannot take anything from it. And in al-Jami': A mukatab confessed to his master while healthy for one thousand dirhams, and the master had written kitabah for him for one thousand, and the mukatab confessed while healthy to an outsider for one thousand dirhams. Then the mukatab fell sick, and he had one thousand dirhams in his hand, so the master collected it from the mukatab, then he died from that illness with no other wealth. So the one thousand is divided between the master and the outsider into three shares: two shares for the master, one share for the outsider. And if the mukatab paid the one thousand to the master from the debt he confessed, then died, the outsider is more entitled to this one thousand, and the master's debt and kitabah become void. And if he died insolvent, he returns to slavery and dies as the master's property, and the master's debt and kitabah become void. And if the master did not receive the one thousand and died leaving it, it belongs to the outsider. And if the mukatab left a son born during kitabah, the outsider is more entitled to this one thousand as well, the master [takes] the son of the mukatab and sells for the debt and kitabah, and if the son pays the kitabah and the debt, the judgment for the outsider is not rescinded. And if a man wrote kitabah for his slave while healthy for one thousand dirhams, and an outsider lent him one thousand dirhams, then the mukatab fell sick and lent him a dirham in the presence of witnesses, then it was stolen from the mukatab, and in the mukatab's hand was another one thousand dirhams, so the master collected it: the master has more right to it than the outsider, unlike if the mukatab bought a slave from the master for one thousand dirhams in his illness, and an outsider has a claim of one thousand against the mukatab, and the slave perished, and the mukatab had one thousand dirhams in hand, so the master collected it from the price of the slave, then the mukatab died from that illness leaving no payment: what the master received from the price of the slave does not become secure for the master, even if the sale and receipt of price were in the presence of witnesses; so the one thousand is taken back and given to the outsider. The difference is that the form of the loan is manifest similitude, so the master is preferred, while it does not appear in the form of sale, so the outsider is preferred. Ponder. And in it also: A man wrote kitabah for his slave for two thousand, and he has two free sons who are his heirs. The mukatab fell sick and confessed to one of the sons for one thousand dirhams, and confessed to the master for a debt of one thousand, then died leaving two thousand dirhams. So the master is more entitled to the two thousand; he collects one for the kitabah and the other for the debt. If he left less than two thousand, he begins with the son's debt. The difference is that if he left two thousand, it is possible to consider him free after death by looking at the form of what was paid, even if it differs in the manner of payment, so the master is preferred because the kitabah contract was in the form of two thousand; unlike when he left less, that is not possible, so the son is preferred. Ponder.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage collects several rulings from Sharh al-Tahawi, al-Muhit, and al-Jami' on various situations involving a mukatab. The first ruling: if a master frees his mukatab while sick, and the manumission is within one-third of the estate, the mukatab becomes free without payment; if it is exactly one-third and heirs do not approve, the mukatab has an option (according to Imam Abu Hanifa) to work for either two-thirds of his value or two-thirds of the kitabah debt. The text clarifies that when the master says 'his slave,' it implies full ownership, distinguishing cases of joint ownership. Then from al-Muhit: if a slave is co-owned by a healthy and a sick person, the healthy one can write kitabah with the sick one's permission, and heirs cannot revoke it even after the sick one's death. Next, from al-Jami': a complex case where a mukatab confesses debts to both his master and an outsider while healthy, then falls ill and the master collects the money in hand; if the mukatab dies insolvent, the master's debt and kitabah are voided, and the outsider gets priority. Another scenario: if the mukatab has a son born during kitabah, the outsider's claim takes precedence over the master's. Then a comparison between a loan and a sale: in a loan scenario with witnesses, the master's claim is preferred; in a purchase scenario, the outsider's claim is preferred. Finally, a case where a mukatab has two heirs (sons) and confesses debts; if he leaves exactly the kitabah amount, the master collects both the kitabah and the debt; if less, the son's debt is paid first. The underlying logic is whether the mukatab can be considered to have died free or in slavery, affecting priority.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave under a kitabah contract, working to earn freedom.
كتابة (kitabah): The contract of gradual manumission where the slave pays installments.
الثلث (al-thulth): One-third of the estate, the maximum allowable for bequests without heirs' consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the ruling from Sharh al-Tahawi, when does a mukatab have the option to work for either two-thirds of his value or two-thirds of the kitabah debt?
A) When the sick master frees him and the value is within one-third of the estate
B) When the sick master frees him and the value is exactly one-third and the heirs do not approve
C) When the sick master frees him and the heirs approve regardless of the amount
D) Whenever a master frees his mukatab, regardless of sickness

Key Takeaway
A sick master's freeing of his mukatab is a bequest; if exactly one-third and heirs reject, the mukatab chooses between two payment options.

Kitabah with Deferred Payment When Heirs Disapprove
First matn: deferred kitabah with heirs' disapproval.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a slave is given kitabah for less than his value with a deferred term and the heirs do not approve, and explain the consequence for the slave.

Core Idea
Deferred kitabah at a discount requires immediate payment of two-thirds of the value or return to slavery.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the matn regarding kitabah (a contract of manumission by payment). When a sick master writes kitabah for a slave at a price less than the slave's market value and with deferred payment, the heirs may object. The commentary explains the outcome: the slave must pay two-thirds of the value immediately or revert to slavery. This rule is by consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The master is in his final illness (marad al-mawt). He writes kitabah for his slave for one thousand dirhams, payable in one year, while the slave's market value is two thousand. The heirs do not approve the transaction.
The deferred term and discount reduce the estate, harming heirs.
2
Determine the slave's obligation
The slave must immediately pay two-thirds of the market value (i.e., 1333.33 dirhams) to the heirs. If he cannot, he returns to slavery.
Two-thirds is used because the master's bequest is limited to one-third of the estate in illness.
3
Understand the consensus
This ruling is by consensus (ijma) among the scholars. It is not disputed.
The commentary says 'bil-ijma' wa qad taqaddama bayanuhu.
4
Apply to modern context
In modern contexts, the principle applies when a terminally ill person makes a contract that reduces the estate; creditors or heirs have rights. The slave's position is unique but analogous to a debt obligation.

العبد فهو مكاتب اختلف الشارحون في صورتها قال بعضهم : قال حر لمولى العبد كاتب عبد على ألف درهم على أني إن أديت لك ألفاً فهو حر فكاتبه المولى على يعتق بأدائه بحكم الشرط، فإذا قبل العبد صار مكاتباً يعني وإن أداه بغير ضمان لا لأنه يرجع تبرع به. هذا إذا أدى عنه بدل الكتابة كلها، وإن أدى عنه البعض فله أن يرجع سواء أداه بضمان أو بغير ضمان لأنه لم يحصل له غرضه وهو العتق فكان حكم الأداء موقوفاً فيرجع، ولو أدى قبل إجازة العبد ثم أجاز ليس له أن . يرجع سواء أدى البعض أو الكل إلا إذا أداه عن ضمان لأن الضمان فاسد فيرجع بحكم فساده. فإن قيل : ما الفرق بين هذا وبين البيع فإن بيع الفضولي لا يتوقف على إجازة He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if he wrote kitabah for him for one thousand with a term of one year, and his value is two thousand, and the heirs do not approve, he pays two-thirds of the value immediately, otherwise he is returned to slavery. This is by consensus and has been explained previously.) He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (A free person wrote kitabah for a slave for one thousand and paid; he becomes free. And if the slave accepts, he is a mukatab.) The commentators differed on its form. Some said: A free person said to the master of the slave: Write kitabah for the slave for one thousand dirhams on the condition that if I pay you one thousand, he is free. So the master wrote kitabah for him—he becomes free by his payment by virtue of the condition. And if the slave accepts, he becomes a mukatab. This contract has two aspects: it is effective regarding what benefits the slave (that he becomes free upon fulfilling the condition) and suspended upon the ratification of the one who has the right to ratify. So if he (the slave) accepts, he becomes a mukatab because ratification at the end is like permission at the beginning. And some said its form is: He says: Write kitabah for your slave for one thousand dirhams, and he does not say: on condition that if I pay you one thousand dirhams he is free. Then if he pays, he does not become free by qiyas because the contract is suspended and the suspended has no effect, and there is no condition. By istihsan, he becomes free. The basis of istihsan is that there is no harm to the slave in his freedom by the payment of the outsider, and the payer does not have recourse against the slave because he (the payer) achieved his objective, which is the freedom of the slave. And it is said that he has recourse against the master and recovers what he paid if he paid under a guarantee, because his guarantee was void, just as if he guaranteed in a sound [contract], he recovers what he paid; so this is more appropriate. And if he paid without a guarantee, he does not have recourse because he donated. This is if he paid the entire kitabah price. If he paid part of it, he has recourse, whether he paid under guarantee or without guarantee, because he did not achieve his objective, which is freedom, so the payment is suspended and he recovers. And if he paid before the slave's ratification and then he ratified, he cannot recover whether he paid part or all, except if he paid under a guarantee, because the guarantee is void, so he recovers due to its invalidity. If it is said: What is the difference between this and sale? For the sale of a fuduli does not depend on the ratification of the ratifier regarding what is for him and what is against him, and here it does not depend regarding what is for him? The answer: What is for him is pure relinquishment, and that does not depend on acceptance. And in the Sharh: If the slave says 'I do not accept,' and the outsider for whom the kitabah was written pays on his behalf, it is not valid because he (the slave) refused. And if a man guarantees, nothing is incumbent upon him because guarantee for the kitabah price is not valid. And in al-Muhit: If this slave is a son of this speaker, and likewise if a young son is a slave of one man, and he writes kitabah for him on behalf of his father, it is not valid because he has no guardianship over his young son when writing kitabah for a slave belonging to another. And if he pays, the slave becomes free in all these cases because we consider the kitabah effective regarding his wealth. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya: A man wrote kitabah for a slave belonging to another by the order of the slave's owner for one thousand dirhams, then he reduced five hundred, and the owner learned and ratified; the kitabah is for five hundred. And if...
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is the sharh (commentary) on two matn statements from Kanz al-Daqaiq. The first matn: if kitabah is written for a deferred term (one year) and the slave's value exceeds the debt, but the heirs do not approve (because it may reduce their inheritance), the slave must immediately pay two-thirds of his value; otherwise he returns to slavery. This is by consensus. The second matn deals with a free person (not the master) writing kitabah for a slave belonging to someone else, paying the price, and the slave becomes free; and if the slave accepts, he becomes a mukatab. The commentators differ on the precise scenario. One interpretation: the free person makes a conditional offer to pay the kitabah price in exchange for the slave's freedom; if the master accepts and the slave agrees, it is valid. Another interpretation: the free person simply asks the master to write kitabah without condition, and then pays; by qiyas, the slave does not become free because the contract is suspended, but by istihsan he becomes free because there is no harm. The commentary then discusses recourse: if the free person paid the entire kitabah price, he cannot recover from the slave (since the slave benefits), but he may have recourse against the master if he paid under a void guarantee. If he paid only part, he can recover because his objective (full freedom) was not achieved. The passage also addresses the difference between this kitabah and a fuduli sale: in kitabah, the benefit to the slave (freedom) is a pure relinquishment that does not require acceptance. Finally, several extensions: if the slave refuses, the payment is invalid; if the free person is the slave's father, he cannot act for his minor son; and if the master ratifies a reduction, the kitabah is for the reduced amount. The text cuts off at the end.

Key Terms
كتابة (kitabah): A contract between a master and a slave whereby the slave earns his freedom by paying a specified sum.
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): Terminal illness; a condition that restricts a person's legal capacity to dispose of wealth beyond one-third.
ثلث القيمة (thulth al-qeemah): Two-thirds of the slave's market value; the amount the slave must pay to the heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The full kitabah price
B) Two-thirds of the kitabah price
C) Two-thirds of the slave's market value
D) The full market value

Key Takeaway
A slave under deferred kitabah from a terminally ill master must pay two-thirds of his market value immediately if the heirs object, or else be enslaved.

Fuduli Kitabah: Qiyas vs Istihsan and Recourse
Second matn: free person writes kitabah for another's slave; qiyas vs istihsan and recourse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between qiyas and istihsan rulings when a free person (fuduli) writes kitabah for another's slave and pays the price, and determine when the payer can recover the paid amount.

Core Idea
By istihsan, a fuduli's payment for kitabah frees the slave; recourse depends on guarantee and completeness of payment.

The second matn deals with a free person who, without prior authorization, writes kitabah for a slave belonging to another and pays the entire price. The commentators analyze whether the slave becomes free. Analogically (qiyas), the slave should not become free because the contract is suspended. However, by istihsan (juridical preference), the slave is freed because there is no harm. The passage then details when the payer can recover the money: if he paid the full amount with a void guarantee, he can recover from the master; if without guarantee, he donated. If he paid only part, he can always recover because his objective (full freedom) was not achieved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fuduli kitabah scenario
A free person (not the master) says to the master of a slave: 'Write kitabah for your slave for 1000 dirhams (with or without a condition).' The master writes it. The free person pays the 1000 dirhams. The slave then accepts or ratifies.
The free person is acting as fuduli (unauthorized) regarding the master's right.
2
Apply qiyas to the fuduli payment
By qiyas on fuduli sale, the contract is suspended (mawquf). Since there is no condition or ratification, the payment has no effect, so the slave does not become free.
Qiyas: fuduli sale is suspended entirely; here payment alone cannot transfer freedom.
3
Apply istihsan to override qiyas
By istihsan, the slave becomes free because there is no harm to anyone (the master receives payment, the slave gains freedom). The payer's objective is achieved, and freedom is a pure relinquishment that does not require acceptance.
Istihsan is based on the absence of harm and the general benefit.
4
Analyze the payer's recourse rights
If the free person paid the entire kitabah price under a void guarantee (daman fasid), he can recover from the master. If he paid without guarantee, he cannot recover because it is a donation. If he paid only part (whether with guarantee or not), he can always recover because his objective (full freedom) was not achieved.
The key: full payment with void guarantee -> recourse; full payment without guarantee -> no recourse; partial payment -> recourse.
5
Distinguish from fuduli sale
In fuduli sale, both rights and obligations are suspended until ratification. Here, the benefit to the slave (freedom) is a pure relinquishment of the master's right, which does not require acceptance; hence it is not suspended.
This distinction explains why the fuduli's payment can be effective by istihsan.

هذا قال رحمه الله : (وإن كاتبه على ألف إلى سنة وقيمته ألفان ولم تجز الورثة أدى ثلثي القيمة حالاً وإلا رد رقيقاً وهذا بالإجماع وقد تقدم بيانه قال رحمه الله : (حر كاتب عن عبد على ألف وأدى عتق وإن قبل العبد فهو مكاتب اختلف الشارحون في صورتها قال بعضهم : قال حر لمولى العبد كاتب عبد على ألف درهم على أني إن أديت لك ألفاً فهو حر فكاتبه المولى على يعتق بأدائه بحكم الشرط، فإذا قبل العبد صار مكاتباً يعني هذا العقد له جهتان نافذ في حق ما ينتفع العبد وهو أن يعتق عند أداء الشرط وموقوف على إجازة من له الإجازة فإذا قبله صار مكاتباً لأن الإجازة في الانتهاء كالإذن في الابتداء. وقال بعضهم صورتها: أن يقول كاتب عبدك على ألف درهم ولم يقل على أني إن أديت لك ألف درهم فهو حر، فإذا أدى لا يعتق قياساً لأن العقد موقوف والموقوف لا حكم له ولم يوجد التعليق، وفي الاستحسان يعتق. وجه الاستحسان أنه لا ضرر على العبد في عتقه بأداء الأجنبي ولا يرجع الدافع على العبد لأنه حصل له مقصوده وهو عتق العبد، وقيل يرجع على المولى ويسترد ما أداه إن أداه بضمان لأن ضمانه كان باطلاً كما لو ضمن في الصحيحة فإنه يرجع بما أدى فهذا أولى، وإن أداه بغير ضمان لا لأنه يرجع تبرع به. هذا إذا أدى عنه بدل الكتابة كلها، وإن أدى عنه البعض فله أن يرجع سواء أداه بضمان أو بغير ضمان لأنه لم يحصل له غرضه وهو العتق فكان حكم الأداء موقوفاً فيرجع، ولو أدى قبل إجازة العبد ثم أجاز ليس له أن . يرجع سواء أدى البعض أو الكل إلا إذا أداه عن ضمان لأن الضمان فاسد فيرجع بحكم فساده. فإن قيل : ما الفرق بين هذا وبين البيع فإن بيع الفضولي لا يتوقف على إجازة المجيز فيما له وفيما عليه وهنا لم يتوقف فيما له والجواب أن ما له هذا إسقاط محض وهو لا يتوقف على القبول. وفي الشارح ولو قال العبد لا أقبل فأدى عنه الأجنبي الذي كاتب عنه لا يجوز لأنه ارتد برده، ولو ضمن الرجل لم يلزمه شيء لأن الكفالة ببدل الكتابة لا تجوز. وفي المحيط : ولو كان هذا العبد ابناً لهذا القائل وكذا لو كان ابن صغير عبداً لرجل واحد فكاتبه عن أبيه لم يجز لأنه لا ولاية له على ابنه الصغير إذا كاتب عبداً للغير وإن أدى عتق العبد في الفصول كلها لأنا اعتبرنا الكتابة نافذة في حق ماله وفي التتارخانية : رجل كاتب عبد الغير بأمر صاحب العبد على ألف درهم ثم حط عنه خمسمائة فبلغ المولى فأجاز فالكتابة بخمسمائة، ولو
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if he wrote kitabah for him for one thousand with a term of one year, and his value is two thousand, and the heirs do not approve, he pays two-thirds of the value immediately, otherwise he is returned to slavery. This is by consensus and has been explained previously.) He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (A free person wrote kitabah for a slave for one thousand and paid; he becomes free. And if the slave accepts, he is a mukatab.) The commentators differed on its form. Some said: A free person said to the master of the slave: Write kitabah for the slave for one thousand dirhams on the condition that if I pay you one thousand, he is free. So the master wrote kitabah for him—he becomes free by his payment by virtue of the condition. And if the slave accepts, he becomes a mukatab. This contract has two aspects: it is effective regarding what benefits the slave (that he becomes free upon fulfilling the condition) and suspended upon the ratification of the one who has the right to ratify. So if he (the slave) accepts, he becomes a mukatab because ratification at the end is like permission at the beginning. And some said its form is: He says: Write kitabah for your slave for one thousand dirhams, and he does not say: on condition that if I pay you one thousand dirhams he is free. Then if he pays, he does not become free by qiyas because the contract is suspended and the suspended has no effect, and there is no condition. By istihsan, he becomes free. The basis of istihsan is that there is no harm to the slave in his freedom by the payment of the outsider, and the payer does not have recourse against the slave because he (the payer) achieved his objective, which is the freedom of the slave. And it is said that he has recourse against the master and recovers what he paid if he paid under a guarantee, because his guarantee was void, just as if he guaranteed in a sound [contract], he recovers what he paid; so this is more appropriate. And if he paid without a guarantee, he does not have recourse because he donated. This is if he paid the entire kitabah price. If he paid part of it, he has recourse, whether he paid under guarantee or without guarantee, because he did not achieve his objective, which is freedom, so the payment is suspended and he recovers. And if he paid before the slave's ratification and then he ratified, he cannot recover whether he paid part or all, except if he paid under a guarantee, because the guarantee is void, so he recovers due to its invalidity. If it is said: What is the difference between this and sale? For the sale of a fuduli does not depend on the ratification of the ratifier regarding what is for him and what is against him, and here it does not depend regarding what is for him? The answer: What is for him is pure relinquishment, and that does not depend on acceptance. And in the Sharh: If the slave says 'I do not accept,' and the outsider for whom the kitabah was written pays on his behalf, it is not valid because he (the slave) refused. And if a man guarantees, nothing is incumbent upon him because guarantee for the kitabah price is not valid. And in al-Muhit: If this slave is a son of this speaker, and likewise if a young son is a slave of one man, and he writes kitabah for him on behalf of his father, it is not valid because he has no guardianship over his young son when writing kitabah for a slave belonging to another. And if he pays, the slave becomes free in all these cases because we consider the kitabah effective regarding his wealth. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya: A man wrote kitabah for a slave belonging to another by the order of the slave's owner for one thousand dirhams, then he reduced five hundred, and the owner learned and ratified; the kitabah is for five hundred. And if...
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is the sharh (commentary) on two matn statements from Kanz al-Daqaiq. The first matn: if kitabah is written for a deferred term (one year) and the slave's value exceeds the debt, but the heirs do not approve (because it may reduce their inheritance), the slave must immediately pay two-thirds of his value; otherwise he returns to slavery. This is by consensus. The second matn deals with a free person (not the master) writing kitabah for a slave belonging to someone else, paying the price, and the slave becomes free; and if the slave accepts, he becomes a mukatab. The commentators differ on the precise scenario. One interpretation: the free person makes a conditional offer to pay the kitabah price in exchange for the slave's freedom; if the master accepts and the slave agrees, it is valid. Another interpretation: the free person simply asks the master to write kitabah without condition, and then pays; by qiyas, the slave does not become free because the contract is suspended, but by istihsan he becomes free because there is no harm. The commentary then discusses recourse: if the free person paid the entire kitabah price, he cannot recover from the slave (since the slave benefits), but he may have recourse against the master if he paid under a void guarantee. If he paid only part, he can recover because his objective (full freedom) was not achieved. The passage also addresses the difference between this kitabah and a fuduli sale: in kitabah, the benefit to the slave (freedom) is a pure relinquishment that does not require acceptance. Finally, several extensions: if the slave refuses, the payment is invalid; if the free person is the slave's father, he cannot act for his minor son; and if the master ratifies a reduction, the kitabah is for the reduced amount. The text cuts off at the end.

Key Terms
فضولي (fuduli): One who acts on behalf of another without authorization; in this context, the free person who writes kitabah for a slave not his own.
استحسان (istihsan): Juridical preference; a method of reasoning that deviates from strict qiyas in favor of a more equitable outcome.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee or suretyship; here, it refers to a guarantee to pay the kitabah price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A free person pays the full kitabah price for a slave without any guarantee. By istihsan, what is the ruling on the slave's freedom and the payer's right to recover?
A) Slave free; payer can recover from master
B) Slave not free; payer can recover from master
C) Slave free; payer cannot recover
D) Slave not free; payer loses the money

Key Takeaway
A fuduli's payment for kitabah frees the slave by istihsan, but the payer's right to recover depends on guarantee status and completeness of payment.

Two Interpretations of the Free Person's Kitaba
Explains two interpretations of the kitaba form by a fuduli.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two interpretations of the free person's kitaba and explain the legal effect of the slave's acceptance.

Core Idea
The free person's kitaba has two forms: one with ta'liq and one without; both lead to the slave's freedom.

The matn states that when a free person contracts kitaba for another's slave and pays, the slave is freed; if the slave accepts, he becomes a mukatab. The commentators differed on the exact wording of the kitaba. This lesson unpacks these two interpretations and the role of the slave's acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two interpretations
Read the passage: some commentators say the free person explicitly conditions his payment (ta'liq), others say he simply offers a kitaba without condition.
The first interpretation involves a condition, the second does not.
2
Analyze the first interpretation (with ta'liq)
The free person says: 'Write a kitaba for your slave for a thousand on the condition that if I pay you a thousand, he is free.' Here the master's acceptance creates a contract, and the slave is freed upon payment by virtue of the condition.
The contract is effective regarding the slave's freedom (what benefits him) but suspended regarding obligations.
3
Analyze the second interpretation (without ta'liq)
The free person says: 'Write a kitaba for your slave for a thousand' without any condition. By qiyas (analogy), payment does not free the slave because the contract is suspended. But by istihsan, the slave is freed.
Istihsan overrides qiyas here for the benefit of the slave.
4
Effect of the slave's acceptance
In both interpretations, if the slave accepts the kitaba (after being informed), he becomes a mukatab. Acceptance later is like permission at the beginning, making the contract effective in all aspects.
The slave's acceptance is crucial for his becoming a mukatab and for the full obligations of kitaba.
5
Distinguish freedom vs. mukatab status
The slave can be freed (by the free person's payment) without becoming a mukatab. Acceptance is required for mukatab status, which entails obligations (like earning and paying installments).
Freedom is a direct effect of payment, while mukatab status is a contractual relationship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الشرط، فإذا قبل العبد صار مكاتباً يعني هذا العقد له جهتان نافذ في حق ما ينتفع العبد وهو أن يعتق عند أداء الشرط وموقوف على إجازة من له الإجازة فإذا قبله صار مكاتباً لأن الإجازة في الانتهاء كالإذن في الابتداء. وقال بعضهم صورتها: أن يقول كاتب عبدك على ألف درهم ولم يقل على أني إن أديت لك ألف درهم فهو حر، فإذا أدى لا يعتق قياساً لأن العقد موقوف والموقوف لا حكم له ولم يوجد التعليق، وفي الاستحسان يعتق. العتق فكان حكم الأداء موقوفاً فيرجع، ولو أدى قبل إجازة العبد ثم أجاز ليس له أن يرجع سواء أدى البعض أو الكل إلا إذا أداه عن ضمان لأن الضمان فاسد فيرجع بحكم فساده. فإن قيل : ما الفرق بين هذا وبين البيع فإن بيع الفضولي لا يتوقف على إجازة المجيز فيما له وفيما عليه وهنا لم يتوقف فيما له والجواب أن ما له هذا إسقاط محض وهو لا يتوقف على القبول. وفي الشارح ولو قال العبد لا أقبل فأدى عنه الأجنبي الذي كاتب عنه لا يجوز لأنه ارتد برده، ولو ضمن الرجل لم يلزمه شيء لأن الكفالة ببدل الكتابة لا تجوز. وفي المحيط : ولو كان هذا العبد ابناً لهذا القائل وكذا لو كان ابن صغير عبداً لرجل واحد فكاتبه عن أبيه لم يجز لأنه لا ولاية له على ابنه الصغير إذا كاتب عبداً للغير وإن أدى عتق العبد في الفصول كلها لأنا اعتبرنا الكتابة نافذة في حق ماله وفي التتارخانية : رجل كاتب عبد الغير بأمر صاحب العبد على ألف درهم ثم حط عنه خمسمائة فبلغ المولى فأجاز فالكتابة بخمسمائة، ولو كان وهب له الألف ثم بلغ المولى فأجاز فالهبة باطلة ولو أن رجلاً كاتب عبد الغير بغير إذنه على ألف درهم فأدى العبد الألف إليه ثم بلغ المولى فأجاز الكتابة جازت الكتابة ولا يجوز الدفع ولا يعتق بذلك الدفع، فإن أجاز المولى الكتابة والدفع فذلك جائز في قول أبي يوسف ويعتق المكاتب بدفعه، ولا تجوز إجازة القبض في قول الإمام وما اكتسبه بعد الكتابة قبل الإجازة فذلك للمكاتب على كل حال .اهـ. وفي شرح الطحاوي ولو كان لرجل عبد غائب فخاطب رجل مولاه فقال كاتب عبدك الغائب على ألف فهذا على وجهين : إما أن يشترط الضمان أو لم يشترط أما إذا لم يضمن فالكتابة جائزة ويتوقف على إجازة العبد، فإن أجازه جاز ولزمه الألف، وإن رده بطل، فلو أن هذا الرجل أدى قبل أن يجيز العبد وقبل أن يفسخ جاز وعتق العبد، وليس له أن يسترد ذلك في الاستحسان اهـ .
A free man wrote a kitaba for a slave for a thousand and paid, the slave is freed; and if the slave accepts, he is a mukatab. The commentators differed about its form. Some said: a free man said to the master of the slave: 'Write a kitaba for the slave for a thousand dirhams on the condition that if I pay you a thousand, he is free.' So the master wrote the kitaba on that condition; he is freed by his payment by virtue of the condition. When the slave accepts, he becomes a mukatab, meaning this contract has two aspects: effective regarding what benefits the slave, that he is freed at the fulfilment of the condition, and suspended subject to the permission of the one who has the right to permit. So if he accepts it, he becomes a mukatab because permission at the end is like permission at the beginning. Others said: its form is that he says: 'Write a kitaba for your slave for a thousand dirhams' and does not say 'on the condition that if I pay you a thousand dirhams he is free.' So if he pays, he is not freed by qiyas because the contract is suspended and the suspended has no ruling, and no condition was found. But by istihsan he is freed. The basis of istihsan is that there is no harm to the slave in his freedom by the payment of a stranger, and the payer does not have recourse against the slave because he achieved his objective—the freeing of the slave. It was said he has recourse against the master and recovers what he paid if he paid with a guarantor, because his guarantee was invalid, as if he gave a surety in a valid sale, then he recovers what he paid, so this is more appropriate. But if he paid without a guarantor, he does not have recourse because he donated it. This is if he paid the entire kitaba amount. If he paid part of it, he has the right to recourse whether he paid with a guarantor or without, because he did not achieve his objective—the freedom—so the ruling of the payment was suspended, so he recovers. And if he paid before the slave's acceptance and then the slave accepted, he does not have the right to recover, whether he paid part or all, unless he paid by a guarantor, because the guarantee is invalid, so he recovers by virtue of its invalidity. If it is said: what is the difference between this and a sale? For the sale of a fuduli (unauthorized agent) is not dependent on the permission of the one with the right regarding what is for him and what is against him, and here it is not dependent regarding what is for him. The answer: what is for him is pure relinquishment, which does not depend on acceptance. In the Sharh: and if the slave said 'I do not accept' and then the stranger who made the kitaba paid for him, it is not permissible because he rejected his rejection. And if a man gave a guarantee, nothing is binding on him because surety for the kitaba payment is not valid. In al-Muhit: and if this slave was a son of this speaker, and similarly if a young son was a slave of one man and he made a kitaba for him on behalf of his father, it is not valid because he has no guardianship over his young son when he makes a kitaba for a slave belonging to another. But if he pays, the slave is freed in all cases because we consider the kitaba effective regarding his property. In al-Tatarkhaniyya: a man made a kitaba for another's slave by order of the slave's owner for a thousand dirhams, then the slave deducted five hundred, and the news reached the master and he permitted it, so the kitaba is for five hundred. And if he had gifted him the thousand and then the master was informed and permitted, the gift is invalid. And if a man made a kitaba for another's slave without his permission for a thousand dirhams, and the slave paid the thousand to him, then the master was informed and permitted the kitaba, the kitaba is valid but the payment is not valid and the slave is not freed by that payment. If the master permits both the kitaba and the payment, that is permissible according to Abu Yusuf and the mukatab is freed by his payment. But according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa), permission of taking payment is not valid, and whatever the slave earned after the kitaba before permission belongs to the mukatab in any case. In Sharh al-Tahawi: and if a man had an absent slave, and another man addressed his master saying: 'Write a kitaba for your absent slave for a thousand.' This has two aspects: either he stipulates a guarantor or not. If he does not stipulate a guarantor, the kitaba is valid and depends on the slave's acceptance. If he accepts, it is valid and the thousand is binding. If he rejects, it is void. If this man pays before the slave accepts and before he rescinds, it is valid and the slave is freed, and he does not have the right to recover that by istihsan.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This is an expansion probe explaining a ruling from the matn. The matn states: 'A free man wrote a kitaba for a slave for a thousand and paid, the slave is freed; and if the slave accepts, he becomes a mukatab.' The commentators (sharihun) differed on the exact scenario. One group says the free man says to the master: 'Write a kitaba for the slave for a thousand on the condition that if I pay you a thousand, he is free.' The master writes the kitaba on that condition. The slave is freed by the free man's payment by virtue of the condition (ta'liq). If the slave accepts the condition, he becomes a mukatab because acceptance later is like initial permission. Another group says the free man simply says 'Write a kitaba for your slave for a thousand' without any condition. By qiyas (analogy), if the free man pays, the slave is not freed because the contract is suspended (mawquf) and a suspended contract has no effect, and there was no ta'liq. However, by istihsan (juristic preference), the slave is freed. The reason (wajh al-istihsan) is that freeing the slave causes no harm to him, and the payer achieves his goal (the slave's freedom). The payer cannot recover the payment from the slave because the slave benefited; but he may recover from the master if he paid with a guarantee (because the guarantee was invalid). The text then discusses various sub-cases: partial payment, payment before acceptance, and compares it to the sale of a fuduli. It also covers scenarios where the slave refuses to accept, and where the slave is the son of the speaker. The ruling from Al-Muhit emphasizes that even if the free man pays without authorization, the slave is freed because the kitaba is considered effective regarding the slave's property. The passage from Al-Tatarkhaniyya deals with a case where the master permits a kitaba made without his permission, and the difference between Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa regarding the validity of the payment. Finally, from Sharh al-Tahawi, a case of an absent slave and the effect of stipulating a guarantor. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that by istihsan, the slave is freed when the free man pays, and if the slave accepts, he becomes a mukatab.

Key Terms
فضولي (fuduli): An unauthorized agent who acts without permission; here the free person acts for the slave without prior acceptance.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas for a more equitable outcome.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first interpretation of the free person's kitaba, what is the effect of the free person's payment?
A) The slave becomes a mukatab immediately.
B) The slave is freed by virtue of the condition.
C) The master must refund the payment.
D) The contract is void.

Key Takeaway
The free person's kitaba can be formed with or without a condition; in both cases, the slave can be freed by istihsan, and acceptance creates a mukatab relationship.

Istihsan and Sub-Cases of Payment in Free Person's Kitaba
Explains the istihsan ruling and sub-cases, including an intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the istihsan reasoning for freeing the slave and describe the effects of payment before acceptance, partial payment, and the intra-Hanafi dispute on master's permission for payment.

Core Idea
Istihsan overrides qiyas: the free person's payment frees the slave, and the payer may recover from the master if he paid with a guarantee.

The passage elaborates on the istihsan ruling that frees the slave despite the suspended contract. It then examines various sub-cases: full payment vs. partial payment, payment before vs. after acceptance, and an intra-Hanafi difference between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding the master's permission for payment. This lesson focuses on these details.

Guided Path
1
Understand the qiyas ruling and its limitation
By qiyas, the slave is not freed because the contract is suspended (mawquf) and no condition was set. However, this leads to hardship.
Qiyas alone would prevent the slave's freedom, which is contrary to the spirit of the law.
2
Appreciate the istihsan reasoning
Istihsan says the slave is freed: there is no harm to the slave, and the payer achieves his objective (freedom). The payer cannot recover from the slave, but may recover from the master if he paid with a (invalid) guarantee.
Istihsan is based on preventing harm and fulfilling the purpose of the act.
3
Analyze payment before acceptance
If the free person pays before the slave accepts, the slave is freed. The payer cannot recover the payment (unless he paid with a guarantee) because his goal is achieved.
Recovery is only possible if the guarantee was invalid; then he can recover from the master.
4
Examine partial payment
If the free person pays only part of the kitaba amount, he can recover the payment regardless of guarantee because he did not achieve his goal (full freedom).
Partial payment does not free the slave, so the payer's objective is thwarted.
5
Review the intra-Hanafi dispute on master's permission
If the master permits both the kitaba and the payment after the fact, Abu Yusuf says the slave is freed and the payment is valid. Abu Hanifa says the permission for payment is not valid, but the slave is still freed (the payment itself is considered).
The dispute affects whether the master can retroactively validate the payment or not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حر كاتب عن عبد على ألف وأدى عتق وإن قبل العبد فهو مكاتب اختلف الشارحون في صورتها قال بعضهم : قال حر لمولى العبد كاتب عبد على ألف درهم على أني إن أديت لك ألفاً فهو حر فكاتبه المولى على يعتق بأدائه بحكم الشرط، فإذا قبل العبد صار مكاتباً يعني هذا العقد له جهتان نافذ في حق ما ينتفع العبد وهو أن يعتق عند أداء الشرط وموقوف على إجازة من له الإجازة فإذا قبله صار مكاتباً لأن الإجازة في الانتهاء كالإذن في الابتداء. وقال بعضهم صورتها: أن يقول كاتب عبدك على ألف درهم ولم يقل على أني إن أديت لك ألف درهم فهو حر، فإذا أدى لا يعتق قياساً لأن العقد موقوف والموقوف لا حكم له ولم يوجد التعليق، وفي الاستحسان يعتق. وجه الاستحسان أنه لا ضرر على العبد في عتقه بأداء الأجنبي ولا يرجع الدافع على العبد لأنه حصل له مقصوده وهو عتق العبد، وقيل يرجع على المولى ويسترد ما أداه إن أداه بضمان لأن ضمانه كان باطلاً كما لو ضمن في الصحيحة فإنه يرجع بما أدى فهذا أولى، وإن أداه بغير ضمان لا لأنه يرجع تبرع به. هذا إذا أدى عنه بدل الكتابة كلها، وإن أدى عنه البعض فله أن يرجع سواء أداه بضمان أو بغير ضمان لأنه لم يحصل له غرضه وهو العتق فكان حكم الأداء موقوفاً فيرجع، ولو أدى قبل إجازة العبد ثم أجاز ليس له أن يرجع سواء أدى البعض أو الكل إلا إذا أداه عن ضمان لأن الضمان فاسد فيرجع بحكم فساده. فإن قيل : ما الفرق بين هذا وبين البيع فإن بيع الفضولي لا يتوقف على إجازة المجيز فيما له وفيما عليه وهنا لم يتوقف فيما له والجواب أن ما له هذا إسقاط محض وهو لا يتوقف على القبول. وفي الشارح ولو قال العبد لا أقبل فأدى عنه الأجنبي الذي كاتب عنه لا يجوز لأنه ارتد برده، ولو ضمن الرجل لم يلزمه شيء لأن الكفالة ببدل الكتابة لا تجوز. وفي المحيط : ولو كان هذا العبد ابناً لهذا القائل وكذا لو كان ابن صغير عبداً لرجل واحد فكاتبه عن أبيه لم يجز لأنه لا ولاية له على ابنه الصغير إذا كاتب عبداً للغير وإن أدى عتق العبد في الفصول كلها لأنا اعتبرنا الكتابة نافذة في حق ماله وفي التتارخانية : رجل كاتب عبد الغير بأمر صاحب العبد على ألف درهم ثم حط عنه خمسمائة فبلغ المولى فأجاز فالكتابة بخمسمائة، ولو كان وهب له الألف ثم بلغ المولى فأجاز فالهبة باطلة ولو أن رجلاً كاتب عبد الغير بغير إذنه على ألف درهم فأدى العبد الألف إليه ثم بلغ المولى فأجاز الكتابة جازت الكتابة ولا يجوز الدفع ولا يعتق بذلك الدفع، فإن أجاز المولى الكتابة والدفع فذلك جائز في قول أبي يوسف ويعتق المكاتب بدفعه، ولا تجوز إجازة القبض في قول الإمام وما اكتسبه بعد الكتابة قبل الإجازة فذلك للمكاتب على كل حال .اهـ. وفي شرح الطحاوي ولو كان لرجل عبد غائب فخاطب رجل مولاه فقال كاتب عبدك الغائب على ألف فهذا على وجهين : إما أن يشترط الضمان أو لم يشترط أما إذا لم يضمن فالكتابة جائزة ويتوقف على إجازة العبد، فإن أجازه جاز ولزمه الألف، وإن رده بطل، فلو أن هذا الرجل أدى قبل أن يجيز العبد وقبل أن يفسخ جاز وعتق العبد، وليس له أن يسترد ذلك في الاستحسان اهـ .
A free man wrote a kitaba for a slave for a thousand and paid, the slave is freed; and if the slave accepts, he is a mukatab. The commentators differed about its form. Some said: a free man said to the master of the slave: 'Write a kitaba for the slave for a thousand dirhams on the condition that if I pay you a thousand, he is free.' So the master wrote the kitaba on that condition; he is freed by his payment by virtue of the condition. When the slave accepts, he becomes a mukatab, meaning this contract has two aspects: effective regarding what benefits the slave, that he is freed at the fulfilment of the condition, and suspended subject to the permission of the one who has the right to permit. So if he accepts it, he becomes a mukatab because permission at the end is like permission at the beginning. Others said: its form is that he says: 'Write a kitaba for your slave for a thousand dirhams' and does not say 'on the condition that if I pay you a thousand dirhams he is free.' So if he pays, he is not freed by qiyas because the contract is suspended and the suspended has no ruling, and no condition was found. But by istihsan he is freed. The basis of istihsan is that there is no harm to the slave in his freedom by the payment of a stranger, and the payer does not have recourse against the slave because he achieved his objective—the freeing of the slave. It was said he has recourse against the master and recovers what he paid if he paid with a guarantor, because his guarantee was invalid, as if he gave a surety in a valid sale, then he recovers what he paid, so this is more appropriate. But if he paid without a guarantor, he does not have recourse because he donated it. This is if he paid the entire kitaba amount. If he paid part of it, he has the right to recourse whether he paid with a guarantor or without, because he did not achieve his objective—the freedom—so the ruling of the payment was suspended, so he recovers. And if he paid before the slave's acceptance and then the slave accepted, he does not have the right to recover, whether he paid part or all, unless he paid by a guarantor, because the guarantee is invalid, so he recovers by virtue of its invalidity. If it is said: what is the difference between this and a sale? For the sale of a fuduli (unauthorized agent) is not dependent on the permission of the one with the right regarding what is for him and what is against him, and here it is not dependent regarding what is for him. The answer: what is for him is pure relinquishment, which does not depend on acceptance. In the Sharh: and if the slave said 'I do not accept' and then the stranger who made the kitaba paid for him, it is not permissible because he rejected his rejection. And if a man gave a guarantee, nothing is binding on him because surety for the kitaba payment is not valid. In al-Muhit: and if this slave was a son of this speaker, and similarly if a young son was a slave of one man and he made a kitaba for him on behalf of his father, it is not valid because he has no guardianship over his young son when he makes a kitaba for a slave belonging to another. But if he pays, the slave is freed in all cases because we consider the kitaba effective regarding his property. In al-Tatarkhaniyya: a man made a kitaba for another's slave by order of the slave's owner for a thousand dirhams, then the slave deducted five hundred, and the news reached the master and he permitted it, so the kitaba is for five hundred. And if he had gifted him the thousand and then the master was informed and permitted, the gift is invalid. And if a man made a kitaba for another's slave without his permission for a thousand dirhams, and the slave paid the thousand to him, then the master was informed and permitted the kitaba, the kitaba is valid but the payment is not valid and the slave is not freed by that payment. If the master permits both the kitaba and the payment, that is permissible according to Abu Yusuf and the mukatab is freed by his payment. But according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa), permission of taking payment is not valid, and whatever the slave earned after the kitaba before permission belongs to the mukatab in any case. In Sharh al-Tahawi: and if a man had an absent slave, and another man addressed his master saying: 'Write a kitaba for your absent slave for a thousand.' This has two aspects: either he stipulates a guarantor or not. If he does not stipulate a guarantor, the kitaba is valid and depends on the slave's acceptance. If he accepts, it is valid and the thousand is binding. If he rejects, it is void. If this man pays before the slave accepts and before he rescinds, it is valid and the slave is freed, and he does not have the right to recover that by istihsan.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This is an expansion probe explaining a ruling from the matn. The matn states: 'A free man wrote a kitaba for a slave for a thousand and paid, the slave is freed; and if the slave accepts, he becomes a mukatab.' The commentators (sharihun) differed on the exact scenario. One group says the free man says to the master: 'Write a kitaba for the slave for a thousand on the condition that if I pay you a thousand, he is free.' The master writes the kitaba on that condition. The slave is freed by the free man's payment by virtue of the condition (ta'liq). If the slave accepts the condition, he becomes a mukatab because acceptance later is like initial permission. Another group says the free man simply says 'Write a kitaba for your slave for a thousand' without any condition. By qiyas (analogy), if the free man pays, the slave is not freed because the contract is suspended (mawquf) and a suspended contract has no effect, and there was no ta'liq. However, by istihsan (juristic preference), the slave is freed. The reason (wajh al-istihsan) is that freeing the slave causes no harm to him, and the payer achieves his goal (the slave's freedom). The payer cannot recover the payment from the slave because the slave benefited; but he may recover from the master if he paid with a guarantee (because the guarantee was invalid). The text then discusses various sub-cases: partial payment, payment before acceptance, and compares it to the sale of a fuduli. It also covers scenarios where the slave refuses to accept, and where the slave is the son of the speaker. The ruling from Al-Muhit emphasizes that even if the free man pays without authorization, the slave is freed because the kitaba is considered effective regarding the slave's property. The passage from Al-Tatarkhaniyya deals with a case where the master permits a kitaba made without his permission, and the difference between Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa regarding the validity of the payment. Finally, from Sharh al-Tahawi, a case of an absent slave and the effect of stipulating a guarantor. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that by istihsan, the slave is freed when the free man pays, and if the slave accepts, he becomes a mukatab.

Key Terms
فضولي (fuduli): An unauthorized agent who acts without permission; here the free person acts for the slave without prior acceptance.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas for a more equitable outcome.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if a free person pays the full kitaba amount before the slave accepts, and the slave later accepts, when can the free person recover the payment?
A) Always, because the payment was made without authorization.
B) Never, because the payment is considered a donation.
C) Only if he paid with a guarantee ( ضمان ).
D) Only if the master permits the payment.

Key Takeaway
The istihsan ruling frees the slave; the payer's right of recourse depends on whether full freedom is achieved and whether he paid with a guarantee.

Rulings on the Absent Slave in Kitaba and Kitaba of an Umm Walad with Sons
Exposition of rulings on absent slave's acceptance, joint kitaba, and mother writing for herself and young sons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the acceptance of an absent slave is void and why a kitaba by an umm walad for herself and her children is valid by istihsan, and state the practical consequences.

Core Idea
The absent slave's consent is not required; the umm walad's kitaba for her children is valid by istihsan, overriding qiyas.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into two interconnected rulings: the voidness of an absent slave's acceptance in a joint kitaba, and the permissibility of a female slave (umm walad) writing kitaba for herself and her young sons. Both rulings hinge on the concept of dependency (taba'iyyah) and the use of istihsan to override strict analogy. The commentator provides detailed reasoning and practical scenarios to illustrate these principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core rulings
Locate the two main rulings: (1) the absent slave's acceptance is void, (2) the umm walad's kitaba for herself and her sons is valid. Note the legal basis (istihsan) given for the second.
2
Understand the qiyas argument
Recognize that qiyas would invalidate the umm walad's kitaba because she lacks guardianship over her children. The same qiyas would also invalidate the absent slave's inclusion, but the passage shows how istihsan overrides.
Qiyas is the baseline, istihsan is the exception.
3
Analyze the istihsan reasoning
See how the Hanafi jurists use istihsan to validate these contracts: the children enter as dependents (tabi'), analogous to the absent slave. The master is compelled to accept payment due to necessity (idtirar) of the payer seeking freedom.
Istihsan is preferred over qiyas due to need and benefit.
4
Examine the practical consequences
Note the effects: neither co-mukatib has recourse against the other for payments; the absent slave is not liable; the children's earnings are their own; if a parent dies, the child pays immediately. These illustrate the application of the rulings.
These consequences flow from the principle of dependency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بشيء ولا يؤاخذ الغائب بشيء وقبوله لغو وإن كاتب الأمة عن نفسها وعن ابنين صغيرين لها صح وأي أدى لم يرجع. الحاضر وفي الكتابة عتقا لوجود شرط عتقهما ويجبر المولى على القبول، أما إذا دفع الحاضر فلأن البدل عليه، وأما إذا دفع الغائب فلأنه ينال به شرف الحرية فيجبر المولى على القبول لكونه مضطراً كما إذا أدى ولد المكاتبة فإنه يجبر على القبول وإن لم يكن البدل عليه، وكمعير الرهن إذا دفع الدين إلى المرتهن يجبر على القبول لحاجته إلى استخلاص حقه وإن لم يكن عليه دين . المحيط : ولو كاتب عبدين كتابة واحدة فارتد أحدهما قيل لا يعتق الحي ما لم يؤد جميع الكتابة كما لو مات أحدهما حتف أنفه أو قتل وإن ترك المقتول كسباً في ردته أخذ المولى منه جميع البدل وعتقا لأن كسبه تعلق به حق الورثة فلم يصر فيئاً، وإذا التحق بدار الحرب أخذ البدل بجميع ويرجع على المرتد بحصته إذا عاد قال رحمه الله: (ولا يرجع على صاحبه بشيء) يعني لا يرجع واحد منهما بما أدى من البدل على الآخر؛ أما الحاضر فلأنه قضی دین نفسه، وأما الغائب فلكونه أدى بغير أمره وليس بمضطر فيه لأنه يطلب نفعاً مبتدأ بخلاف معير الرهن فلأنه مضطر من جهته قال في المحيط كاتب عبدين على ألف منجمة كتابة واحدة فزاد أحدهما مائة درهم ولم يقبل الآخر الزيادة فإنه يلزم الزائد نصف الزيادة ويكون عليه حالاً ويعتقان بأداء الألف لأن الزيادة لم تلتحق بأصل العقد لأن الكتابة المنجمة تعليق والتعليق لا يحتمل التغير فإذا أدى أحدهما لا يرجع بها على الآخر لأنه تبرع. ولو زاد أحدهما مائة وضمها فالزيادة كلها عليه نصفها بالأصالة ونصفها بالكفالة . قال رحمه الله : (ولا يؤاخذ الغائب بشيء) يعني لا يطالب المولى الغائب ببدل الكتابة لأنه لا دين عليه لأنه لم يلتزم بشيء وإنما دخل في الكتابة تبعاً فصار نظير ولد المكاتبة . قال رحمه الله: (وقبوله لغو) يعني قبول الغائب ورده لغو لأن الكتابة قد نفذت وتمت من غير قبوله فلا يعتبر بعد ذلك قبوله لا رده كمن كفل ديناً عن غيره بغير أمره فبلغه فإجازته باطلة ولا يتغير حكمه حتى لو له أدى لا يرجع . قال رحمه الله : (وإن كاتب الأمة عن نفسها وعن ابنين صغيرين لها صح) وهذا استحسان، والقياس أن لا يجوز وقد ذكرنا وجهه في مسألة الغائب لأن هذه مثلها في جميع ما ذكرنا من الأحكام لما أن الأم والأب الرقيق لا ولاية له على ولده فيكون دخول الولد في كتابتهما بالشرط لا بالولاية كدخول الغائب في كتابة الحاضر وقبول الأولاد وردهم وفي المحيط : كاتب عبده وامرأته على أنفسهما وأولادهما الصغار، ثم إن إنساناً قتل الولد فقيمته للأبوين ولو غاب الأب فأراد المولى استسعاء الولد في شيء من الكتابة لم يكن له ذلك ولا سبيل للأبوين على كسب الولد لأنه مكاتب أصلاً بخلاف المولود في الكتابة لأنه دخل تبعاً فكان كسبه تبعاً. ويدفع حصته عن الأبوين إن أعتقه السيد، وإن مات الأبوين أدى حالاً. يعتبر.
Nothing, and the absent one is not held liable for anything, and his acceptance is void. If a female slave writes a kitaba for herself and her two young sons, it is valid. And whichever one pays does not have recourse. The present one and in the kitaba become free because the condition of their freedom is present, and the master is compelled to accept. As for when the present one pays, because the payment is upon him; and as for when the absent one pays, because he obtains the honor of freedom through it, so the master is compelled to accept due to his necessity, just as when the child of a female mukatib pays, the master is compelled to accept even though the payment is not upon him. And like the lender of a pawn: if he pays the debt to the pledgee, he is compelled to accept due to his need to reclaim his right, even though he is not indebted. Al-Muhit: If a person writes a single kitaba for two slaves, and one of them apostatizes, it is said that the living one does not become free until he pays the entire kitaba, just as if one of them died a natural death or was killed. And if the killed slave left earnings during his apostasy, the master takes the entire payment from it and they both become free, because his earnings had the right of the heirs attached to them, so they did not become fay'. And if he joins dar al-harb, the master takes the entire payment, and he has recourse against the apostate for his share if he returns. He (the author) said: 'And neither one has recourse against the other for anything.' That is, neither of them has recourse against the other for what he paid of the payment. As for the present one, because he paid his own debt; as for the absent one, because he paid without his order and is not in a state of necessity in doing so, because he seeks a new benefit, unlike the lender of a pawn because he is in necessity from his side. He said in al-Muhit: Two slaves write a single kitaba for one thousand dirhams in installments, then one of them adds one hundred dirhams and the other does not accept the increase: the one who added is liable for half the increase, and it becomes due immediately, and they both become free upon payment of the thousand, because the increase did not attach to the original contract because an installment kitaba is a ta'liq, and ta'liq does not allow change. So if one pays, he does not have recourse against the other for it because he gave a donation. If one added one hundred and included it, the entire increase is upon him, half originally and half as guarantor. He (the author) said: 'And the absent one is not held liable for anything.' That is, the master does not demand the absent one for the kitaba payment, because there is no debt upon him, as he did not undertake anything; he only entered the kitaba as a dependent, so he becomes like the child of a female mukatib. He (the author) said: 'And his acceptance is void.' That is, the absent one's acceptance and rejection are void, because the kitaba has been executed and completed without his acceptance, so his acceptance or rejection after that is not considered, like one who guarantees a debt for another without his order, then it reaches him: his ratification is invalid and its ruling does not change. So even if he pays, he does not have recourse. He (the author) said: 'And if a female slave writes a kitaba for herself and her two young sons, it is valid.' This is istihsan, and qiyas is that it is not valid. We have mentioned its justification in the issue of the absent one, because this is like it in all the rulings we mentioned, because the mother and the enslaved father have no guardianship over their child, so the child's inclusion in their kitaba is by condition, not by guardianship, like the inclusion of the absent one in the kitaba of the present one, and the acceptance and rejection of the children. And in al-Muhit: If he writes a kitaba for his slave and his wife for themselves and their young children, then a person kills one of the children, his value is for the parents. And if the father is absent and the master wants to make the child earn towards something of the kitaba, he does not have the right to do so. And the parents have no claim on the child's earnings because he is a mukatib originally, unlike a child born during the kitaba, because he entered dependently, so his earnings are dependent. And he pays his share on behalf of the parents if the master frees him. And if both parents die, he pays immediately. It is considered.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of various rulings related to the kitaba contract, particularly concerning the absent slave (al-gha'ib) and the case of a female slave (umm walad) writing kitaba for herself and her young sons. The commentator explains each ruling with legal reasoning and analogies.

The first ruling: The absent slave's acceptance or rejection of the kitaba is void (laghw). The kitaba is valid without his consent because he enters as a dependent. The master is compelled to accept payment from either the present or the absent slave. If the present pays, it's because the payment is his obligation; if the absent pays, it's because he seeks the benefit of freedom, creating necessity (idtirar) analogous to the lender of a pawn who pays the debt to retrieve his collateral.

Then the passage discusses two slaves on a single kitaba: if one apostatizes, the other must pay all to become free, just as if one dies. The earnings of the apostate are taken by the master to pay the kitaba because the rights of heirs are attached. If the apostate joins dar al-harb, the master takes the payment and has recourse against him later.

The author then clarifies that neither slave has recourse against the other for payments made; the present pays his own debt, the absent pays voluntarily without necessity. The same applies if one adds extra to the kitaba: the increase is his donation, and he cannot recover it.

The ruling that the absent is not held liable (la yu'akhadhu al-gha'ib) reiterates that he has no debt, being a dependent. His acceptance is void because the contract is already complete.

Finally, the case of a female slave (or umm walad) writing kitaba for herself and her young sons: this is valid by istihsan. The qiyas would invalidate it because the mother has no guardianship over her children, but istihsan permits it because the children enter as dependents, analogous to the absent slave. The children's inclusion is by condition, not authority. Various consequences are detailed: earnings belong to the children as original mukatibs, and they pay their share if the mother is freed, etc. The passage ends with the note that if the child was born after the kitaba, his earnings are dependent on the parents.

This is a typical Hanafi expansion that shows how istihsan overrides qiyas in certain cases to facilitate the contract's objectives.

Key Terms
الغائب (al-gha'ib): The slave who is absent at the time of the kitaba contract; his acceptance is considered void because the contract is completed without him.
المكاتب (al-mukatib): Slave who is in a kitaba contract to earn freedom by paying installments.
استحسان (istihsan): Preferring a ruling due to equity and necessity, overriding qiyas (analogy).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under Hanafi law, what is the status of the acceptance of an absent slave in a kitaba contract made by a present co-owner?
A) It is valid and required.
B) It is void (laghw).
C) It is optional.
D) It must be sought later.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the absent slave's consent is irrelevant, and a mother can contract kitaba for her dependents by istihsan, overriding the analogy of guardianship.

Joint Mukatabah Freed by One Co-owner: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Divisibility of Manumission
Ruling on joint mukatabah freed by one co-owner with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on divisibility of manumission (i'taq) in the case of a joint mukatabah and apply the ruling on guaranty (daman) to a similar scenario.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa holds manumission divisible; the Sahibayn hold it indivisible, leading to different remedies for co-owners.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding a joint female slave who is made a mukatabah and later freed by one co-owner. When she becomes unable to pay the kitabah installments, the ruling on guaranty depends on whether manumission is considered divisible or indivisible. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi distinction between daman i'taq (guaranty of manumission) and daman tamalluk (guaranty of ownership).

Guided Path
1
State the Abu Hanifa position
Identify the ruling given by Imam Abu Hanifa when a wealthy co-owner frees his share of a mukatabah slave who later becomes unable to pay.
He holds that the manumitter guarantees half the value to the partner and recovers it from the slave.
2
State the Sahibayn position
Identify the ruling given by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) in the same scenario.
They hold that the manumitter does not recover from the slave; instead, the silent partner compels istis'a if the manumitter is insolvent.
3
Identify the underlying principle – divisibility of manumission
Recognize that the disagreement stems from whether manumission (i'taq) is divisible (yatajazzau) or indivisible.
The Sahibayn hold it is indivisible; Abu Hanifa holds it is divisible.
4
Analyze the effect of the dispute on guaranty
Understand how the divisibility principle leads to different outcomes: if divisible, only the manumitter's share is freed initially, and the kitabah remains for the other half; if indivisible, the entire slave is freed immediately and the kitabah is annulled.
This affects whether the manumitter can recover from the slave and the silent partner's options.
5
Distinguish daman i'taq from daman tamalluk
Note that in the case of tadbir or istilad, the guaranty is daman tamalluk, which is due immediately regardless of wealth, unlike daman i'taq which depends on the manumitter's wealth at the time of freeing.
This distinction is crucial for understanding the different rulings in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كاتباها فحررها أحدهما موسراً فعجزت ضمن لشريكه نصف قيمتها ورجع به عليها وهذا عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : لا يرجع المعتق عليها ويستسعيها الساكت إن كان المعتق معسراً، والأصل في هذا أن الإعتاق لا يتجزئ عندهما والكتابة لا تمنع العتق فعتقت كلها للحال وانفسخت الكتابة، فالحكم عندهما ما تقدم. ومن أصل الإمام أن العتق عنده يتجزئ فجاز إعتاق النصف فلا يؤثر الفساد في نصيب الساكت فلا يضمن العتق قبل العجز لعدم ظهور أثر الإعتاق فيها، فإذا عجزت ظهر أثر العتق وكان للساكت الخيارات المذكورة في العتق وهي إن كان موسراً فله أن أو الضمان، فإذا ضمن كان للمعتق أن يرجع على العبد، وإن كان المعتق معسراً كان له خيار العتق أو الاستسعاء على ما بينا في العتق وعلى هذا الخلاف لو دبرها واستولدها فإذا عجزت ظهر أثرهما فيضمن قيمتها موسراً كان أو معسراً لأن هذا ضمان تملك . لا يتجزئان فصارت كلها أم الولد أو مدبرة ويضمن لشريكه نصف قيمتها في الحال موسراً كان أو معسراً لأنه ضمان تملك فلا يختلف بين اليسار والإعسار ويضمن العقر في الاستيلاد.
And if they made her a mukatabah, then one of them freed her while wealthy, and she became unable (to pay), he guarantees half her value to his partner and recovers it from her. This is according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: The manumitter does not recover from her, and the silent partner compels her to earn (istis'a) if the manumitter is insolvent. The principle in this is that manumission is indivisible according to them, and kitabah does not prevent manumission, so she is entirely free immediately and the kitabah is annulled. So the ruling according to them is what preceded. According to Imam's (Abu Hanifa's) principle, manumission is divisible in his view, so manumitting half is permissible; the invalidity does not affect the silent partner's share, so he does not guarantee before incapacity due to absence of the effect of manumission in her. When she becomes incapable, the effect of manumission appears, and the silent partner has the options mentioned in manumission: if he is wealthy, he has the option of (either) or guaranty; if he guarantees, the manumitter can recover from the slave; if the manumitter is insolvent, he has the option of manumission or istis'a, as we explained in manumission. And on this difference, if he made her a mudabbara and she gave birth (istilad), then she became incapable, their effects appear; he guarantees her value whether wealthy or insolvent because this is a guaranty of ownership. They (the two causes) are indivisible, so she becomes entirely an umm walad or mudabbara, and he guarantees half her value to his partner immediately, whether wealthy or insolvent, because it is a guaranty of ownership, so it does not differ between wealth and insolvency, and he guarantees the 'aqr (dower) in istilad.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a joint female slave who is made a mukatabah (contract of kitabah) and then freed by one of the co-owners while he is wealthy. Later she becomes unable to pay the kitabah installments. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the manumitter must guarantee half her value to his partner and can recover that amount from the slave. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the manumitter does not recover from the slave; instead, the silent partner can compel her to earn (istis'a) if the manumitter is insolvent. The basis of the disagreement is the divisibility of manumission: the Sahibayn hold that manumission is indivisible, so once one co-owner freed her, she becomes entirely free immediately and the kitabah is annulled. Abu Hanifa holds that manumission is divisible, so only half of her is freed, and the kitabah remains valid for the other half. The effect of manumission only appears when she becomes unable to pay, at which point the silent partner has options (guaranty, manumission, or istis'a). The same principle applies if the slave was made a mudabbara (tadbir) or gave birth (istilad). If she becomes unable, the effects of both causes appear, and since each cause is indivisible, she becomes fully a mudabbara or umm walad. The manumitter guarantees half her value immediately, regardless of wealth, because this is a guaranty of ownership, not of manumission. He also guarantees the 'aqr (compensation for intercourse) in case of istilad.

Key Terms
الإعتاق لا يتجزئ (al-i'tiq la yatajazzau): Manumission is indivisible; if a co-owner frees his share, the entire slave is freed and the other co-owner loses his share without compensation except as stated.
ضمان تملك (daman tamalluk): Guaranty for ownership; when one co-owner causes the slave's status to change (e.g., tadbir or istilad) affecting the other's share, he must pay the value immediately regardless of wealth.
مكاتبة (mukatabah): A female slave under a kitabah contract, allowed to earn and pay installments to buy her freedom.
استسعاء (istis'a'): Compelling a slave to work to earn money to pay off a debt or value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what happens when a co-owner frees his share of a mukatabah slave and she later becomes unable to pay?
A) The slave is entirely free immediately and the kitabah is annulled.
B) The manumitter guarantees half the value to his partner and recovers it from the slave.
C) The silent partner must accept istis'a if the manumitter is wealthy.
D) The manumitter does not have to pay anything because the kitabah prevents freedom.

Key Takeaway
The divisibility of manumission is the key principle determining the remedies for co-owners of a joint mukatabah slave freed by one partner.
