Joint Slave: Tadbir and Manumission – Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Divisibility
Ruling on a joint slave with tadbir and manumission, and the divisibility debate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's position on the divisibility of tadbir and explain the mudabbir's options when the co-owner frees the joint slave.

Core Idea
Tadbir is divisible per Abu Hanifa; the mudabbir can demand guaranty from the manumitter for the value of his share.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a joint slave where one co-owner makes a deferred manumission (tadbir) and the other co-owner then frees the slave outright. The ruling hinges on whether tadbir is divisible: Imam Abu Hanifa holds it is, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it is indivisible. Understanding this dispute reveals the legal options available to the mudabbir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and actions
The scenario involves a slave jointly owned by two persons. One co-owner (the mudabbir) declares tadbir (deferred manumission after his death). Then the other co-owner frees the slave while the mudabbir is wealthy (mūsir).
Wealth is a condition because if the mudabbir were insolvent, the manumitter would have no claim.
2
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, tadbir is divisible (yatajazzau). Therefore, the tadbir only affects the mudabbir's own share of the slave. However, it corrupts (yufsid) the other co-owner's share, giving the mudabbir certain options.
The mudabbir's options include demanding guaranty (tadmin), manumitting the slave (i'tāq), or compelling istis'ā' (earning freedom).
3
Analyze the effect of the manumission
When the other co-owner frees the slave, the mudabbir loses the options of guaranty and istis'ā' but retains the right to demand guaranty for his own share as a mudabbir. He can claim half the slave's value (as a mudabbir) from the manumitter.
The mudabbir does not become owner of the other share via guaranty; the slave remains joint property but the mudabbir's share is now free.
4
Examine the Sahibayn's view (indivisibility)
The Sahibayn hold that tadbir is indivisible. In a related case (if the slave were a mukatab), they rule that the tadbir makes the entire slave a mudabbir for the one who declared it, and he can own the other share by paying its value. This is triggered automatically, not by option.
This view is mentioned in the text as a comparison, not the main ruling for the joint slave case.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilāf)
Under Abu Hanifa, the mudabbir has options (including guaranty) after the manumission. Under the Sahibayn, in the mukatab case, the mudabbir automatically owns the whole by paying value. The main case of a regular joint slave is not explicitly ruled by the Sahibayn, but the principle of indivisibility would lead to different outcomes.
The text presents Abu Hanifa's view as the relied-upon position for the main scenario.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عبد لهما دبره أحدهما ثم حرره الآخر موسراً للمدبر أن يضمن المعتق نصف قيمته) وهذا عند الإمام ووجهه أن التدبير يتجزئ عنده فيقتصر التدبير على نصيب المدبر لكن يفسد به نصيب الآخر فيثبت خيار التضمين أو الإعتاق أو الاستسعاء على ما عرف من مذهبه، فإذا أعتق لم يبق له خيار التضمين والاستسعاء فيقتصر على نصيبه لأنه يتجزئ عنده لكن يفسد نصيب الآخر فله أن يضمنه نصيبه وله خيار العتق والاستسعاء، فإذا ضمنه يضمنه قيمة نصيبه مدبراً وقد عرف قيمة المدبر في بابه وإذا ضمنه لا يتملكه بالضمان لأنه لا يقبل النقل من ملك إلى ملك كما إذا غصب مدبراً وأبق وضمن الغاصب قيمته فإنه لا يتملكه كذا هذا. قيد بقوله ثم حرره الآخر فعلم أنه من لأنه لو لم يكن قناً قال في المحيط : مكاتب بين رجلين دبر أحدهما صار الكل مديراً له وهو مكاتب له عندهما ويتملكه بالقيمة للشريك موسراً كان أو معسراً، لأن التدبير لا يتجزئ عندهما فتدبيره لا في نصيب شريكه، فإذا تملكه يتملك بضمان القيمة وضمان القيمة لا يختلف باختلاف اليسار والإعسار. واختلفوا أنه يضمن قيمته مكاتباً أو قناً؛ قيل يغرم نصف قيمته قناً لأنه تنفسخ الكتابة في نصيب شريكه فسخ الكتابة لا يتجزئ، وقيل يضمن قيمته مكاتباً لأن الفسخ إنما لا يحتمل التجزئ لضرورة تضاد الأحكام في محل واحد وذلك لا يوجد هنا فإن الكل قد صار مدبراً من جهة المدبر.
A slave belonging to both of them: one made him a mudabbir (deferred manumission), then the other freed him while wealthy. The mudabbir can demand from the manumitter guaranty of half his value. This is according to Imam (Abu Hanifa). Its reasoning is that tadbir is divisible in his view, so tadbir is confined to the mudabbir's share but it corrupts the other's share, so the options of guaranty, manumission, or istis'a are established as known from his madhhab. When he frees, he no longer has options of guaranty and istis'a, so he is confined to his share because it is divisible in his view, but it corrupts the other's share, so he can demand guaranty of his share and has the options of manumission or istis'a. If he demands guaranty, he guarantees the value of his share as a mudabbir, and the value of a mudabbir is known in its chapter. And if he guarantees, he does not become owner through the guaranty because it does not accept transfer from ownership to ownership, just as if someone usurped a mudabbir and it ran away and the usurper guaranteed its value, he does not become owner. This is similar. The qualification 'then the other freed him' indicates that he is (free) because if he were not a slave, al-Muhit says: A mukatab belonging to two men, one made him a mudabbir, becomes entirely a mudabbir for him, and he is a mukatab for him according to them, and he becomes owner by value for the partner, whether wealthy or insolvent, because tadbir is indivisible in their view, so his tadbir does not affect his partner's share. When he becomes owner, he becomes owner by guaranty of value, and guaranty of value does not differ between wealth and insolvency. They differed on whether he guarantees his value as a mukatab or as a slave; some said he pays half his value as a slave because the kitabah is annulled in his partner's share, and annulment of kitabah is indivisible; some said he guarantees his value as a mukatab because the annulment does not accept division due to necessity of conflicting rulings in one place, and that is not present here because the entire (slave) has become a mudabbir from the side of the mudabbir.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage deals with a joint slave where one co-owner makes him a mudabbir (deferred manumission after death) and then the other co-owner frees him while wealthy. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the mudabbir can demand that the manumitter guarantee half the slave's value. The reasoning is that tadbir is divisible in Abu Hanifa's view. Therefore, the tadbir only affects the mudabbir's share, but it corrupts the other share (makes it invalid). The mudabbir initially has options (guaranty, manumission, istis'a) on the other share. However, when the other co-owner actually frees the slave, the mudabbir loses the options of guaranty and istis'a, and only has the option to demand guaranty of his share (now as a mudabbir) or to free or compel istis'a. If he chooses guaranty, he guarantees the value of his share as a mudabbir (not as a regular slave). But this guaranty does not transfer ownership to him because a mudabbir is not transferable by nature; it's similar to a usurper who guarantees a mudabbir that ran away. The text also discusses a different scenario: if the slave were a mukatab and one did tadbir, according to the Sahibayn, the entire slave becomes a mudabbir for that co-owner and he remains a mukatab for the other, and the mudabbir can own the other share by paying its value (guaranty), which is the same whether wealthy or insolvent. There is a difference of opinion on whether he pays value as a mukatab or as a slave; the preferred view is that he pays as a mukatab because annulment of kitabah in the partner's share does not require indivisibility here.

Key Terms
التدبير يتجزئ (al-tadbir yatajazzau): Tadbir (deferred manumission after master's death) is divisible, so it can affect only one co-owner's share.
خيار التضمين (khiyar al-tadmin): The option to demand guaranty from the co-owner who acted (manumitted or caused tadbir) for the value of the other's share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the key difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding tadbir on a joint slave?
A) Abu Hanifa says tadbir is invalid; Sahibayn say it is valid.
B) Abu Hanifa says tadbir is divisible; Sahibayn say it is indivisible.
C) Abu Hanifa says the mudabbir automatically owns the whole; Sahibayn say he does not.
D) Abu Hanifa says the manumitter must pay full value; Sahibayn say half value.

Key Takeaway
The divisibility of tadbir determines the mudabbir's rights: Abu Hanifa gives him an option for guaranty, while the Sahibayn's indivisibility leads to automatic ownership in certain cases.

Joint Slave: Manumission Then Tadbir — Liability and Options
Ruling on joint slave: manumission then tadbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the liability of co-owners when one frees a joint slave and the other later performs tadbir, and distinguish between the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
When manumission precedes tadbir, the manumitter is not liable; the mudabbir's options are restricted.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents a reverse scenario of co-ownership: one co-owner frees his share, and then the other makes the slave a mudabbir. The ruling hinges on whether the tadbir can attach after partial freedom, and whether the manumitter must compensate. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two students (Sahibayn) differ on the validity of the tadbir and resulting liability. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies how the Hanafi school handles the intersection of manumission and tadbir in joint ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sequence of actions
What is the order of events? First, one co-owner (the manumitter) frees his share of the joint slave. Then, the other co-owner performs tadbir (declares the slave free after his death).
The order is crucial: manumission before tadbir.
2
State the ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa
The manumitter is not liable for any guaranty. The mudabbir retains only the options of manumitting the remaining share or requiring the slave to earn his value (istis'a); he loses the option to demand guaranty from the manumitter.
Abu Hanifa considers the tadbir valid and effective.
3
State the ruling according to the Sahibayn
The tadbir is completely invalid because manumission is indivisible: once the first co-owner freed his share, the entire slave becomes free. Hence no ownership remains for tadbir to attach. The one who performed tadbir must pay the full value of the slave to the manumitter if he (the mudabbir) is wealthy.
This is a case of daman i'taq (guaranty for manumission).
4
Analyze the reasoning behind each view
Abu Hanifa: Manumission can be partial (only the manumitter's share is freed, the other share remains in corrupt ownership). Tadbir is valid and changes the mudabbir's options. Sahibayn: Manumission is indivisible; freeing one share frees the whole slave, so there is no ownership for tadbir.
The core difference: divisibility of manumission.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under Abu Hanifa, the mudabbir does not pay and retains control over the remaining share. Under Sahibayn, the mudabbir must pay the entire value if wealthy, and the slave is fully free.
The difference affects the financial liability of the mudabbir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن حرره أحدهما ثم دبره الآخر لا يضمن المعتق لأن المدبر كان له الخيارات السابقة فإذا دبره لم يبق له خيار التضمين وبقي خيار العتق والاستسعاء وهذا عند الأمام. وعندهما تدبير الثاني باطل لأن الإعتاق لا يتجزئ عندهما فيعتق كله فلم يصادف التدبير الملك ويضمن قيمته إن كان موسراً لأن هذا ضمان إعتاق فيختلف بين اليسار والإعسار والله تعالى أعلم.
And if one of them freed him, then the other made him a mudabbir, the manumitter does not guarantee. Because the mudabbir had the previous options; when he made him a mudabbir, he no longer has the option of guaranty, and the options of manumission and istis'a remain. This is according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa). According to them (the Sahibayn), the tadbir of the second is invalid because manumission is indivisible according to them, so he is entirely free, so the tadbir did not coincide with ownership, and he guarantees his value if he is wealthy because this is a guaranty of manumission, which differs between wealth and insolvency. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage addresses a reverse scenario: a joint slave is freed by one co-owner, and then the other co-owner makes him a mudabbir. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the manumitter does not have to guarantee anything to the mudabbir. The reasoning: after the manumitter freed his share (and the entire slave became free due to the Sahibayn's view or because of Abu Hanifa's view that the manumitter's share is freed, but the other share remains corrupt?), the mudabbir (the one who did tadbir later) loses his option to demand guaranty because he already performed tadbir, and he only retains the options to free or do istis'a (if the manumitter is insolvent). According to the Sahibayn, the tadbir of the second is completely invalid because manumission is indivisible; once the first co-owner freed, the entire slave became free, so there was no ownership left for the tadbir to attach. In that case, the second co-owner (who attempted tadbir) must guarantee the value of the slave to the first if he (the second) is wealthy, because this is a guaranty of manumission (daman i'taq) which depends on wealth.

Key Terms
ضمان إعتاق (daman i'taq): Guaranty for manumission: when someone causes the freeing of a slave belonging to another, he must pay the value if he is wealthy.
تدبير (tadbir): A form of manumission where a master declares his slave free after the master's death; it is a suspended manumission.
استسعاء (istis'a): Requiring a slave to earn a certain amount to purchase his own freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If one co-owner frees a slave and then the other does tadbir, what is the ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) The manumitter must guarantee the value to the mudabbir.
B) The mudabbir's tadbir is valid and he becomes owner of the manumitter's share.
C) The manumitter is not liable, and the mudabbir retains only the options of manumission or istis'a.
D) The slave is entirely free and the tadbir is valid as a bequest.

Key Takeaway
When manumission precedes tadbir in a joint slave, Imam Abu Hanifa holds the manumitter not liable, while the Sahibayn invalidate the tadbir and impose daman i'taq on the mudabbir if wealthy.

Delay in declaring mukatab incapable when property is pending
Ruling on respite for mukatab with pending property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on giving a mukatab a three-day respite when he cannot pay an installment but claims property will arrive, and explain the intra-Hanafi difference with Abu Yusuf's position.

Core Idea
A mukatab who cannot pay but expects property gets a three-day respite by istihsan—not wajib.

When a mukatab (a slave under a contract of manumission) is unable to pay an installment but claims he has property that will arrive soon, the judge must decide whether to annul the kitabah immediately or grant a delay. This lesson explains the Hanafi ruling: a recommended three-day respite based on istihsan (juristic preference), and contrasts it with Abu Yusuf's stricter view requiring two consecutive unpaid installments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mukatab's situation
The mukatab has defaulted on an installment but asserts he has property that will arrive (e.g., money owed to him or goods in transit). This is not a case of complete inability.
The default is real but there is a reasonable expectation of payment.
2
State the immediate ruling
The judge does not declare the mukatab incapable immediately. Instead, he grants a respite of up to three days (or two to three days, as stated in al-Bada'i').
The three-day period is analogized to the respite given to a debtor for payment.
3
Explain the legal basis: istihsan
Waiting is recommended (mustahabb) by istihsan, not obligatory (wajib). The judge may choose not to wait, but it is better to do so. The obligation to annul is not enforced during this period.
If the property arrives within three days, the kitabah continues; if not, the judge annuls.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the judge should not declare incapacity until two consecutive installments are due and unpaid. He cites the saying of Ali (RA): 'If two installments are due on the mukatab consecutively, he is returned to slavery.'
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) disagree, adhering to the three-day rule.
5
Understand the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: three days respite. Abu Yusuf's view is a legitimate ikhtilaf but not the operative position for fatwa.
The text does not explicitly favor one view, but the structure of the discussion indicates the majority position.

مكاتب عجز عن نجم وله مال سيصل لم يعجزه الحاكم إلى ثلاث أيام) نظراً للجانبين والثلاثة هي المدة التي ضربت لإمهال الأعذار كإمهال الخصم للدفع والمدين للقضاء فلا يزاد عليه قال صاحب العناية : والمدين بالجر عطفاً على كإمهال . أقول: هذا بحسب الظاهر غير صحيح قطعاً لأنا لا نشك أن المديون معطوف على الخصم والمعنى وكإمهال المديون لأجل القضاء ويقبل قوله في الأمهال بمجرد قوله. قال في البدائع : فإن عجز عن نجم فإن كان له مال حاضر أو غائب بأن قال لي مال على إنسان أو قال يجيء في القافلة يمهله القاضي إلى الثلاثة أيام إذ انتظار المدة مندوب قال في البدائع : ينتظر يومين أو ثلاثة استحساناً والواجب لا يجبر فيه ولا يخفى أن النجم هو الطالع وسمي به الوقت المضروب ثم سمي به ما يؤدي من الوظيفة. قال رحمه الله : (وإلا عجزه وفسخها أو سيده برضاه) يعني إذا لم يكن له مال سيصل في ثلاثة أيام فسخ القاضي الكتابة أو فسخ المولى برضا المكاتب وهذا عند الإمام ومحمد وقال أبو يوسف : لا يعجزه حتى يتوالا عليه نجمان لقول علي رضي الله تعالى عنه : إذا تولى على المكاتب نجمان يرد في الرق. والأمر فيما لا
A mukatab who is unable to pay an installment and has property that will arrive, the judge does not declare him incapable until three days, considering both sides. Three is the period set for giving respite for excuses, like giving respite to the opponent for payment and to the debtor for settlement, so it is not increased. The author of al-'Inaya said: 'and the debtor' in the genitive case is coordinated with 'like giving respite'. I say: This is apparently definitely incorrect, because we have no doubt that 'al-madyun' is coordinated with 'al-khasm', and the meaning is: like giving respite to the debtor for the sake of settlement, and his statement about respite is accepted simply by his saying. He said in al-Bada'i': If he is unable to pay an installment, and he has property present or absent, such as saying 'I have money owed to me by someone' or 'it is coming in the caravan', the judge gives him respite up to three days, because waiting for the period is recommended. He said in al-Bada'i': He waits two or three days by istihsan, and the obligatory is not enforced in it. And it is not hidden that 'najm' (star) is the rising (star) and by it the prescribed time is named, then by it the payment of the installment is named. This is according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: He does not declare him incapable until two consecutive installments are due, based on the saying of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): 'If two installments are due on the mukatab consecutively, he is returned to slavery.' Commentary
This passage is the beginning of a new chapter on the death of the mukatab, his incapacity, and death of the master. It first addresses the incapacity of the mukatab who cannot pay an installment but has property that is expected to arrive. The judge is to give him a respite of up to three days before declaring him incapable, as a consideration for both parties. The three-day period is analogized to the respite given to a debtor. There is a grammatical discussion about the phrase 'almadyun' in the text. The author quotes al-Bada'i' stating that if the mukatab claims he has money owed to him or goods coming, the judge gives him two to three days as a matter of istihsan (preference), not as an obligation. The term 'najm' originally refers to a star, then to a set time, and then to the installment amount due at that time. If the mukatab has no imminent property, the judge annuls the kitabah, or the master may annul with the mukatab's consent. This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf disagrees, requiring two consecutive unpaid installments before annulment, citing a hadith from Ali (RA). The text cuts off, but the chapter continues on the next page.

Key Terms
النجم (al-najm): The installment due from the mukatab; also the time prescribed for payment.

Rescission of Kitaba: Grace Period and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on postponing rescission for a mukatab with imminent funds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for judicial rescission of a mukatab contract and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the number of missed stars.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school grants a three-day grace for a mukatab with imminent funds; only one missed star triggers rescission after that.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the procedure when a mukatab fails to pay his installment. The judge does not immediately declare him incapable; instead, a three-day delay is granted if the mukatab has money expected soon. An intra-Hanafi dispute exists between Abu Hanifa (and Muhammad) and Abu Yusuf regarding whether one or two missed payments are required for rescission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The mukatab who fails to pay a star (najm) is not immediately declared incapable. If he has money that will arrive soon, the judge postpones the declaration for three days.
The three-day period is analogized from court procedures for giving opponents respite.
2
Understand the condition of 'imminent funds'
The mukatab must assert that he has money coming, e.g., from a debtor or a caravan. The judge accepts his statement at face value and grants the delay.
If no such assertion or funds, the judge proceeds to rescind.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on number of missed stars
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that one missed star suffices for rescission after the three-day grace. Abu Yusuf requires two consecutive missed stars based on a narration from Ali.
The text prefers the majority view.
4
Examine the judicial role and subsequent effects
The judge must rescind when the master requests and the conditions are met. Upon rescission, the mukatab returns to full slave status and his property belongs to the master.
The kitaba is binding on the master but not on the slave, so the slave can also rescind unilaterally.

Source Text

باب موت المكاتب وعجزه وموت المولى
تأخير باب أحكام هذه الأشياء ظاهر التناسب لأن هذه الأشياء متأخرة عن عقد الكتابة فكذا بيان أحكامها . قال رحمه الله : مكاتب عجز عن نجم وله مال سيصل لم يعجزه الحاكم إلى ثلاث أيام) نظراً للجانبين والثلاثة هي المدة التي ضربت لإمهال الأعذار كإمهال الخصم للدفع والمدين للقضاء فلا يزاد عليه قال صاحب العناية : والمدين بالجر عطفاً على كإمهال . أقول: هذا بحسب الظاهر غير صحيح قطعاً لأنا لا نشك أن المديون معطوف على الخصم والمعنى وكإمهال المديون لأجل القضاء ويقبل قوله في الأمهال بمجرد قوله. قال في البدائع : فإن عجز عن نجم فإن كان له مال حاضر أو غائب بأن قال لي مال على إنسان أو قال يجيء في القافلة يمهله القاضي ورده إلى الرق. والأثر فيه كالمرفوع. وما رواه عن علي : لا ينفي الفسخ إذا عجز عن نجم بل هو سكوت عنه . وأفاد بقوله «أو سيده برضاه أن الكتابة لازمة من جانب المولى غير لازمة من جانب العبد ، فلو أراد العبد لم يرده القاضي في الرق وإن رده لم يكن رداً للآخر حتى لو رجع مسلماً لم يرد إلى مولاه، فلو قال «في كتابة واحدة» لكان أولى اهـ . قال رحمه الله : وعاد أحكام الرق) يعني إذا عجز عاد إلى أحكام الرق لأن Chapter on the Death of the Mukatab, his Inability, and Death of the Master. Delaying the chapter on the rulings of these matters is manifestly appropriate because these matters are subsequent to the contract of kitaba; thus the explanation of their rulings is similar. He (the author) said: A mukatab who is unable to pay a star and has money that will arrive, the judge does not declare him incapable until three days, out of consideration for both sides. And three is the period set for giving respite for excuses, like the respite of the opponent to pay and the debtor to fulfill; so it is not increased. The author of al-Inayah said: 'and the debtor' (is in the genitive) as a conjunct to 'like the respite'. I say: this is evidently incorrect, for we do not doubt that 'the debtor' is conjunct to 'the opponent' and the meaning is: and like the respite of the debtor for the purpose of fulfillment. And his word regarding the respite is accepted upon his mere statement. He said in al-Bada'i: If he is unable to pay a star, and he has present or absent money, saying 'I have money due from someone' or 'it will come in the caravan', the judge gives him a delay of three days, because waiting for the period is recommended. He said in al-Bada'i: He waits two or three days by istihsan, and the obligatory is not enforced. And it is not hidden that 'najm' is the rising star, and is named after the set time, and then named after the amount paid at that time. He said: (Otherwise he declares him incapable and rescinds it, or his master may [rescind] with his consent), meaning that if he has no money arriving within three days, the judge rescinds the kitaba, or the master rescinds with the mukatab's consent. This is according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: He does not declare him incapable until two stars combine upon him, based on the saying of 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): When two stars combine upon the mukatab, he is returned to slavery. The matter is not grasped by qiyas like the khabar, and it is a gracious contract, so much so that the postponement in it is a year. And they have what is narrated from 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him): He rescinded it due to inability to pay a star and returned him to slavery. And the athar is like marfu'. And what he narrated from 'Ali does not negate rescission if unable for a star; rather it is silence about it. And his statement 'or his master with his consent' indicates that the kitaba is binding on the master's side but not binding on the slave's side. So if the slave wants to rescind the kitaba and the master refuses, the slave may do so in the correct narration. The second narration says it is binding on the slave's side as well, so he cannot rescind without the master's consent. And the meaning of his word 'rescinds it' is that the judge rules him incapable because it is obligatory when the master requests, and he has authority over that, even if the slave does not consent; so judgment is necessary like the return due to defect. The apparent meaning of his statement 'a mukatab unable to pay a star' includes when he contracts alone or with others, but it is not so; rather it is specific to when he contracts alone. He said in al-Muhit: If he contracts two slaves as one kitaba and one fails to pay, and the judge returns him to slavery without knowing about the kitaba of the other, then the other performs the kitaba, both become free because the return of the first to slavery was not valid as long as the other is able to pay the kitaba price. For this reason, if the judge knew of the other's kitaba, he does not return until both are together. And if two masters contract a single slave as one kitaba and he fails to pay, he is not returned to slavery until both masters are together, because if one is absent, rescission in the other's share is impossible. And if the master dies leaving heirs, some of them may return [the mukatab] to slavery by judgment, but they do not have that without judgment, because some heirs act as opponent for the deceased in what is for him and against him. In al-Muhit: He contracted his two slaves as one kitaba, then one apostasized and joined the enemy territory, and the present one failed to pay; the judge does not return him to slavery, and if he returns him, it is not a return for the other. Even if the apostate returns as a Muslim, he is not returned to his master. If he had said 'in one kitaba', it would have been better. He said: (And the rulings of slavery return), meaning that when he is incapable, he returns to the rulings of slavery because the kitaba has been rescinded, and the lifting of interdiction was for the sake of the kitaba contract, so it does not remain without the contract. And it is not hidden that the author said 'the rulings of slavery return' and did not say 'returns to slavery' because he remains in it. He said: (And what is in his hand belongs to his master) because it becomes clear that it is the earning of his slave, which was suspended for him or for the master; if he performed, it would be for him, and if he failed, it is for the master. Since inability has been realized, it belongs to his master.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage explains the rulings when a mukatab (slave under contract of manumission) fails to pay a scheduled installment (najm). The matn states that the judge should not immediately declare him incapable; instead, a three-day grace period is granted if the mukatab has money that is expected to arrive. The commentary clarifies that the three-day period is analogized from delaying opponents and debtors in court. Abu Yusuf holds that two consecutive failures are required, based on a statement of 'Ali, but the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) rely on the practice of 'Umar who rescinded after one failure. The passage also discusses that the kitaba is binding on the master but not on the slave, meaning the slave can unilaterally rescind. Furthermore, it covers complex scenarios involving multiple slaves or masters, emphasizing that rescission only fully occurs when all parties are present or have knowledge. Finally, upon rescission, the mukatab returns to full slave status, and any property he possesses belongs to his master.

Key Terms
النجم (al-najm): The installment payment in a kitaba contract; also the time set for payment.
يعجزه (yu'jizuhu): The judge declares the mukatab incapable (ma'juz) of fulfilling the kitaba, leading to rescission.
فسخ الكتابة (faskh al-kitaba): Rescission of the contract of kitaba, returning the slave to full slave status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The mukatab must miss two consecutive stars.
B) The judge must wait three days after the missed star if the mukatab has imminent funds.
C) The master must consent to the rescission.
D) The mukatab must be declared insane.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school balances the master's right and the mukatab's potential by granting a three-day grace; the majority view allows rescission after one missed installment.

Death of Mukatab with Assets: Contract Continues
Ruling and proof that kitaba continues upon death of mukatab with assets

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mukatab's contract when he dies with sufficient assets, explain the qiyas to a sale contract, and evaluate the ikhtilaf regarding hadd for qadhf after payment.

Core Idea
Kitaba is a contract of exchange; like sale, it survives death if the deceased has assets to pay.

Many assume a mukatab's death dissolves the kitaba contract, but Hanafi fiqh treats it as an exchange contract similar to sale. This lesson explains the ruling, the qiyas-based proof, and a related ikhtilaf about hadd punishment for slander after payment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the death of a mukatab who has sufficient wealth to pay the kitaba. The ruling: the kitaba contract is not dissolved; payment is made from his estate, and he is deemed free at the last moment of his life.
The ruling applies only if the mukatab dies with assets ('wafā').
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites qiyas (analogy): kitaba is a contract of exchange (ʿaqd muʿāwaḍah), and such contracts do not dissolve upon the death of either party. The primary example is bayʿ (sale).
The dalil text is: 'أن الكتابة عقد معاوضة لا تنفسخ بموت أحد المتعاقدين كالبيع'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The effective cause (illa) is the exchange nature. Both sale and kitaba involve mutual obligations: payment for ownership of a commodity in sale, payment for freedom in kitaba. Since the illa is identical, the ruling that the contract survives death applies equally.
The analogy is strengthened by noting that the contract remains even after the master's death, so it should remain after the slave's death.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
A sub-discussion: if someone falsely accuses (qadhf) the mukatab after payment, is hadd obligatory? The text mentions a view ('qīla') that hadd is not obligatory because freedom is established retrospectively from the last part of life, implying that the accusation occurred when he was technically still a slave.
The author's wording suggests the preferred view is that hadd is obligatory, as the payment is effective for most rulings.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that the kitaba continues and the successor pays. The alternate view on hadd is a legitimate ikhtilaf, but the stronger position imposes hadd, as the payment has real legal effects.
No tarjih authority is named, but the Zahir al-Riwayah supports the main ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا تفسخ وتؤدي كتابته من ماله وحكم بعتقه في آخر حياته وإن ترك ولداً ولد في كتابته إذا قال أنت حر بعد موتي ولنا أن الكتابة عقد معاوضة لا تنفسخ بموت أحد المتعاقدين وهو المولى فلا ينفسخ بموت الآخر وهو العبد كالبيع ولأن قضية المعاوضة المساواة فإذا بقي العقد بعد موت المولى لحاجته إلى الولاء وغيره جاز أن يبقى بعد موت العبد لحاجته إلى الحرية ليتوصل إلى حرية أولاده، ولو مات عاجزاً تفسخ الكتابة، ولو قذفه إنسان بعد الأداء يلزمه الحد، وقيل الأداء لا يلزمه الحد لأن العتق ثبت مستنداً إلى آخر جزء من أجزاء حياته فلا يظهر الاستناد في حق هذا الحكم. قال رحمه الله : (وتؤدي كتابته من ماله) يعني يؤدي من خلفه فيكون أداء الخليفة كأدائه بنفسه. فإن قيل : الأداء فعل والاستناد يكون في أحكام الشريعة قلنا : نعم لكن فعل الثابت مضافاً إلى حسي الثبوت وهذه الإضافة شرعية ألا ترى أن من رمى صيداً فمات قبل أن يصيبه ثم أصابه صار مالكاً له حتى يورث عنه والمالك ليس بأهل لكن لما صح السبب والملك يثبت بعد تمام السبب وتمامه بالإضافة إليه وهو ليس أهلاً له ثبت الملك من حين الإمكان وهو آخر جزء من أجزاء حياته فكذا هنا.
It is not dissolved, and his kitaba is paid from his wealth, and it is ruled that he is free at the last part of his life. And if he leaves a child born during his kitaba, [and] if he said, 'You are free after my death' – and for us, the kitaba is a contract of exchange, not dissolved by the death of one of the contracting parties, that is the master, so it is not dissolved by the death of the other, the slave, like a sale. And because the requirement of exchange is equality; so if the contract remains after the death of the master due to need for wala' and other things, it is permissible for it to remain after the death of the slave due to need for freedom to reach the freedom of his children. If he dies unable [to pay], the kitaba is dissolved. If someone accuses him of illicit intercourse after payment, hadd is obligatory; it is said that payment does not make hadd obligatory because freedom is established as dependent on the last part of his life, so the dependency does not appear regarding this ruling. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: '(And his kitaba is paid from his wealth)' meaning his successor pays, so the payment of the successor is like his own payment. If it is said: Payment is an act, and dependency occurs in the rulings of Shari'a, we say: Yes, but the act of the confirmed [person] is attributed to the sensory confirmation, and this attribution is Shari'a-based. Do you not see that if someone shoots game and dies before hitting it, then [the arrow] hits it, he becomes its owner such that it is inherited from him, and the owner is not eligible, but because the cause is sound and ownership is established after the completion of the cause and its completion by attribution to him, and he is not eligible, ownership is established from the time of possibility, which is the last part of his life, so likewise here.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The author begins by stating the ruling: if a mukatab dies while having sufficient assets to pay the kitaba, the contract is not dissolved. Instead, the payment is made from his estate, and he is considered free at the last moment of his life. If he leaves a child born during the kitaba, the child is also treated similarly. The phrase 'if he said you are free after my death' seems to refer to a tadbir scenario, but the text is ambiguous. The proof follows: the kitaba is an exchange contract, like a sale, so it does not dissolve upon the death of either party. It remains after the master's death because of the need for wala' and other benefits, and after the slave's death because of the need to achieve freedom for the slave and his children. If the mukatab dies without assets, the kitaba is dissolved. A sub-ruling: if someone falsely accuses the mukatab after payment, hadd is obligatory; however, some say it is not obligatory because the freedom is predicated on the last moment of life and this predication does not apply to this ruling. The commentator then explains that the payment by the successor is like payment by the mukatab himself, using an analogy of a hunter who dies before his arrow hits but still acquires ownership at the last moment.

Key Terms
كتابة (kitābah): A contract between a master and a slave whereby the slave pays a sum in installments and becomes free upon full payment.
عقد معاوضة (ʿaqd muʿāwaḍah): A contract of exchange where each party gives and receives something of value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the kitaba contract if the mukatab dies with sufficient assets to pay?
A) The contract is dissolved immediately.
B) The contract continues and payment is made from his estate.
C) The contract is dissolved but the master may renew it.
D) The contract becomes invalid and the slave remains a slave.

Key Takeaway
Kitaba is a contract of exchange that, like a sale, survives the death of the mukatab if he leaves assets to pay, and the payment by his successor is equivalent to his own payment.

Child of Insolvent Mukatab Must Work to Pay Kitaba
Ruling on child born during kitaba when mukatab dies without assets

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a child born during kitaba when the mukatab dies without assets, and identify the intra-Hanafi differences regarding the umm walad and the option scenario.

Core Idea
The child succeeds the father in the kitaba obligation; if he pays, both are freed.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies what happens when a mukatab (a slave contracted to earn his freedom by installments) dies insolvent but leaves a child born under the same kitaba contract. The matn rules that the child must continue working to fulfill the installments, and upon payment, both father and child are deemed freed. The commentary then explores finer points: whether the child must be from the mukatab's own slave woman, the child's capability, and important intra-Hanafi differences from al-Kafi and al-Muhit regarding the mother's status and the effect of an option clause.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
Read the matn: the child works like his father on the installments. If he pays, the child and father are freed. Note that this assumes the father died without sufficient assets.
The ruling is a continuation of the kitaba obligation.
2
Analyze the condition about the child's origin
The commentator debates whether the child must be from the mukatab's own slave woman or could be from another's. The apparent cause restricts it to his own slave woman because the child entered into his kitaba and his earnings belong to him.
This affects who exactly is obligated.
3
Examine the capability assumption
The matn says 'he works', implying capability. The commentator notes that this is not always necessary; the child may still be obligated even if not fully capable, but the text's wording suggests capability is typical.
Flexibility in application.
4
Study the al-Kafi scenario: option and mother's death
If the master had an option period and the mother dies leaving a child, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the option and kitaba remain, and the child can work (istihsan). Muhammad holds that the kitaba becomes invalid (qiyas).
The dispute is between istihsan and qiyas.
5
Study the al-Muhit scenario: umm walad of mukatab
The mukatab dies leaving an umm walad (slave mother of his child). If she has a child, she is not sold and must work for the kitaba. If no child, Abu Hanifa says she is sold; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say she is not sold and must pay instead.
Disagreement on the basis of the child's presence.
6
Consider the multiple children case
If installments are due on children born during kitaba and some are absent, the present child cannot be enslaved until the absent one returns because dissolving the contract for one would affect all.
Preserves unity of the contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وإن ترك ولداً ولد في كتابته ولا وفاء سعى كأبيه على نجومه فإن أدى حكم بعتقه وعتق أبيه قبل موته وظاهر إطلاق المتن أنه لا فرق بين ما إذا ولد في أمته أو أمة الغير، وظاهر العلة تقييده بالأول لأن الولد دخل في كتابته وكسبه له الأداء فيخلفه في وصار أداؤه كأداء أبيه فجعل كأنه ترك وفاء مع الولد. والظاهر من قوله «يسعى» أن الولد المولود فيها لا بد أن يكون قادراً على السعي وليس كذلك. قال في الكافي : لو كاتب أمته على أنه بالخيار ثلاثة أيام فولدت في مدة الخيار وماتت وبقي الولد يبقي خياره وعقد الكتابة عند الإمام والثاني وله أن يجيزها، وإذا أجاز يسعى الولد على نجوم الأم وإذا أدى عتقت الأم في آخر جزء من أجزاء حياته وعتق ولدها وهذا استحسان، وعند الثالث تبطل الكتابة ولا يصح إجازة المولى وهو القياس. وفي المحيط : ولو ترك أم ولده معها ولد لا تباع واستسعت في الكتابة على نجوم المكاتب وإن لم يكن معها ولد باعها عند الإمام لأن حرية أو الولد لأجل الولد فإذا لم يكن ولد تباع. وعندهما لا تباع وتؤدي بدل الكتابة بعد موت المكاتب كما لو كان معها ولد. ولو حل على أولاده المولودين في الكتابة نجم ولم يؤدوا وبعضهم غائب لم يرد الحاضر في الرق حتى يرجع الغائب لأن الفسخ على الحاضر فسخ على الغائب وقد تعذر في حق الغائب فتعذر في حق
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if he leaves a child born during his kitaba and no ability to pay, he works like his father on his installments. If he pays, it is ruled that he becomes free and his father becomes free before his death. The apparent generality of the text indicates no difference between whether [the child] was born from his slave woman or from another's slave woman, but the apparent cause restricts it to the first because the child entered into his kitaba and his earnings are for him, so he succeeds him, and his payment becomes like the payment of his father, so it is as if he left ability to pay with the child. The apparent meaning of his statement 'he works' is that the child born during it must be capable of working, but that is not the case. He said in al-Kafi: If a man made his slave woman a mukataba on the condition that he has the option for three days, and she gave birth during the option period, and she died, and the child remained, his option and the kitaba contract remain according to Imam [Abu Hanifa] and the second [Abu Yusuf], and he may ratify it. If he ratifies, the child works on the installments of the mother; if he pays, the mother is freed in the last part of his life, and her child is freed. This is istihsan. According to the third [Muhammad], the kitaba becomes invalid and the master's ratification is not valid; that is the qiyas. And in al-Muhit: And if he leaves his umm walad with a child, she is not sold and is made to work for the kitaba on the installments of the mukatab. If she has no child, she is sold according to Imam because the freedom of the mother is due to the child; if there is no child, she is sold. According to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], she is not sold and she pays the kitaba payment after the death of the mukatab as if she had a child. And if an installment becomes due on his children born during kitaba and they do not pay, and some of them are absent, the present one is not returned to slavery until the absent one returns, because dissolving [the contract] for the present is dissolving for the absent, and it is impossible regarding the absent, so it is impossible regarding
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling from the matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) and its commentary. The matn states that if a mukatab dies without sufficient assets but leaves a child born during the kitaba, the child must work to pay the installments as his father did. If the child pays fully, he is freed and his father is deemed free before his death. The commentator discusses whether the child must be from the mukatab's own slave woman or another's, and concludes the apparent cause restricts it to his own. The child's payment is like the father's because the child entered into the same kitaba and his earnings belong to him. The commentator notes that the text says 'he works' implying capability, but this is not always necessary. Then, quoting al-Kafi, there is a scenario where the master had an option, and the mother died giving birth; the ruling depends on which imam's view is followed: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say the kitaba remains and the child can work; Muhammad says it becomes invalid. Then from al-Muhit: The umm walad (mother of a child) of the deceased mukatab: if she has a child, she is not sold and must work; if no child, Abu Hanifa says she is sold, but the two say she is not sold. Finally, a case where multiple children are mukatab and some are absent: the present one cannot be enslaved until the absent one returns, because dissolving for one would dissolve for all, and it is impossible for the absent.

Key Terms
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who has borne a child to her master; she becomes free upon her master's death.
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a kitaba contract to earn freedom by paying installments.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference departing from qiyas for a stronger reason.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning from an established case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) She is sold immediately.
B) She is not sold and is made to work for the kitaba installments.
C) She is freed automatically.
D) She is returned to her former master.

Key Takeaway
The child born during kitaba inherits the obligation to work, but details of the umm walad's fate and the effect of an option clause are subject to legitimate intra-madhhab differences.

Order of Debts Upon a Mukatib's Death
Ruling with proof – debt hierarchy rationale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchy of debts upon a mukatib's death and identify the legal rationale (talil) for the priority.

Core Idea
Debt priority on mukatib's death: loan > jinaaya > kitaba > mahr; each level's strength determines rank.

This passage from al-Muhit establishes a clear hierarchy of debts when a mukatib (a slave under contract of manumission) dies leaving sufficient funds. The ruling is based on the legal strength (quwwa) of each obligation, derived from careful analysis of the nature of each debt. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for correctly distributing the estate and ensuring that the mukatib's freedom is honored.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four debts
List the debts mentioned: loan debt (dayn al-mudāyana), compensation for injury (badal al-jināya), kitaba payment (badal al-kitāba), and dower (mahr) of a woman married without the master's permission.
The passage also discusses a master's debt owed by the mukatib.
2
Understand the basis for hierarchy
The debts are ordered by their legal strength. The stronger debt takes priority. Strength is assessed by how fully each debt represents compensation and by the circumstances under which it was contracted.
The rationale is 'talil' – a reasoned explanation.
3
Analyze each debt's strength
Loan debt is strongest because it is compensation from every aspect. Jinaaya debt is weaker because its substitute (the slave's person) is not property and thus not owned before receipt. Kitaba is weaker than jinaaya because it can be waived by the master upon the slave's incapacity. Mahr is weakest because it was contracted by a slave under interdiction (without the master's permission).
Compare each pair: loan > jinaaya, jinaaya > kitaba, kitaba > mahr.
4
Apply the hierarchy to distribution
When the mukatib dies with sufficient funds, pay debts in order: loan, jinaaya, kitaba, mahr. The remainder is inheritance for his children (who become free by his emancipation). If a separate master's debt exists, pay it after jinaaya but before kitaba, unless kitaba would be left unpaid – then kitaba takes priority to ensure the mukatib dies free.
The master's debt is treated similarly to a loan debt in strength.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
In the case of a jointly owned slave who is made mukatib without the partner's consent, Abu Hanifa holds he dies incapable (half mukatib), while the two disciples (Sahibayn) consider him fully mukatib with earnings belonging to him and requiring compensation to the partner.
The Sahibayn's view is considered mufta bihi in later Hanafi practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط : مات المكاتب عن وفاء يبدئ بالدين ثم ببدل الجناية ثم ببدل الكتابة ثم بمهر امرأة تزوجها بغير إذن مولاه ثم الباقي ميراث بين أولاده الدين عتقوا بعتقه والذين كانوا أحراراً قبله لأن الديون متى اجتمعت يبدئ بالأقوى ودين المداينة أقوى من دين الجناية لأنه عوض من كل وجه، ودين الجناية عوض من وجه لأن مبدله ليس بمال ولهذا لا يملك قبل القبض، ودين الجناية أقوى من بدل الكتابة لأنه لا يسقط بالعجز، ودين الكتابة أقوى من دين المهر لأنه وجب بإذن السيد والمهر وجب بعقد محجور عليه. وإن مات عن وفاء دين المولى يبدئ بدين المولى ثم بالكتابة والباقي ميراث فإن لم يوف بالدين والكتابة بدأ بالكتابة لأنه إذا بدأ بها يموت حراً والولد المولود في الكتابة والولد المكاتب معه كتابة واحدة سيأتي في الإرث لأنهما يعتقان معه في آخر جزء من أجزاء حياته فإن كان الولد منفرداً بالكتابة فأدى بعد موت الأب بعد قضاء مكاتبه الأب أو قبله لم يرث لأنه كان عبداً يوم مات الأب فلم يعتق بعتقه، وإنما عتق بعد موت أبيه . كاتب عبداً مشتركاً بغير إذن شريكه فمات العبد وترك كسباً فقد مات عاجزاً عند الإمام لأن نصفه يصير مكاتباً فلا سبيل لواحد منهما على كسبه. وعندهما كله مكاتب ويكون كل الكسب ملكاً له فيؤدي من كسبه ويضمن المكاتب نصف قيمته لشريكه ا هـ .
And in al-Muhit: A mukatib dies with sufficient estate; he begins with debt, then with the compensation for injury, then with the kitaba payment, then with the dower of a woman he married without his master's permission, then the remainder is inheritance among his children who became free by his emancipation and those who were free before him. Because when debts gather, he begins with the strongest. A loan debt is stronger than a jinaaya debt because it is compensation from every aspect. A jinaaya debt is compensation from one aspect because its substitute is not property, hence it is not owned before receipt. A jinaaya debt is stronger than kitaba payment because it is not waived by incapacity. Kitaba payment is stronger than dower debt because it became obligatory with the master's permission, while dower became obligatory by a contract of one under interdiction. If he dies with sufficient to cover the master's debt, he begins with the master's debt, then kitaba, and the remainder is inheritance. If the kitaba debt is not fully covered, he begins with kitaba because if he begins with it, he dies free. A child born during kitaba and a child who is mukatib with him in one kitaba will come in inheritance because they are freed with him in the last part of his life. If the child is independently under kitaba and performs payment after the father's death after settling the father's kitaba or before, he does not inherit because he was a slave on the day the father died, so he was not freed by his emancipation; he only became free after his father's death. If a man writes a jointly owned slave without the partner's permission, and the slave dies leaving earnings, he died incapable according to Imam Abu Hanifa because half of him becomes mukatib, so neither of them has claim on his earnings. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), all of him is mukatib and all earnings are his property, so he pays from his earnings and the mukatib guarantees half his value to his partner.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage, from al-Muhit, is a ruling on the order of distribution when a mukatib dies leaving sufficient funds to cover all obligations. The source establishes a hierarchy of debts based on their legal strength. Loan debt (dain al-mudayana) is strongest because it is compensation from every aspect. Jinaaya debt (for crimes causing injury) is weaker because its substitute is not property (it is the person himself), so it is not owned before actual receipt. Jinaaya debt is still stronger than kitaba payment because it is not dropped by the slave's incapacity, while kitaba payment can be waived if the slave becomes incapable. Kitaba payment is stronger than mahr debt because kitaba was contracted with the master's permission, whereas mahr was contracted by a slave under interdiction. If the mukatib also owes a debt to his master, that is paid first, then kitaba, then inheritance. If funds are insufficient for both master's debt and kitaba, priority is given to kitaba so the mukatib dies free. The passage also discusses cases of a child born in kitaba and a joint kitaba child, and the ruling when a jointly owned slave is written without the partner's consent: Imam Abu Hanifa considers the slave died incapable (only half mukatib), while the two disciples consider him fully mukatib, with earnings belonging to him and the master guaranteeing half the value to the partner.

Key Terms
دين المداينة (dayn al-mudāyana): A loan debt; an obligation to repay a sum of money borrowed.
بدل الجناية (badal al-jināya): Compensation for a crime causing injury or homicide; blood money or damages.
بدل الكتابة (badal al-kitāba): The payment agreed upon in a kitaba contract; the price of freedom paid in installments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is jinaaya debt weaker than loan debt?
A) It can be waived by the master
B) Its substitute is not property
C) It is contracted under interdiction
D) It is not yet due

Key Takeaway
Debt priority on a mukatib's death is determined by the legal strength of each obligation: loan debt strongest, followed by jinaaya, then kitaba, then mahr.

Child Born in Kitaba: Substitute for Father's Kitaba
Ruling that a child born during the father's kitaba assumes the kitaba obligation upon the father's death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a child born during kitaba assuming the father's obligation and explain the istihsan vs qiyas dispute.

Core Idea
A child born during the father's kitaba steps into the kitaba by istihsan, overriding the qiyas that would void the contract.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses the fate of a kitaba contract when the mukatib dies leaving a child born during the contract. The Hanafi school, by istihsan, allows the child to work and pay the installments, thus freeing both the child and the father posthumously. The commentary expands on the evidence and the intra-madhhab difference between Imam Abu Hanifa (and Abu Yusuf) and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the child's obligation to work on the father's installments. The ruling is that the child assumes the kitaba contract upon the father's death.
The child is not originally a party to the contract.
2
Understand the basis: istihsan vs qiyas
The Hanafi position uses istihsan (juristic preference) to override the strict qiyas that would deny the child's substitution. Qiyas would void the contract because the child was not a party.
Istihsan is a primary Hanafi source that prioritizes equity.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf adopt istihsan; Muhammad al-Shaybani holds to qiyas, declaring the kitaba void. The mufta bihi is the istihsan position.
The dispute is within the school; the relied-upon view is the majority.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Under the istihsan view, the child works and both become free. Under qiyas, the kitaba is lost and the child remains a slave.
Practical consequence: freedom vs continued slavery.
5
Note the conditions and scope
The child must have been born during the kitaba period. The ruling applies even if the child is not capable of working; the obligation is established.
The text clarifies that 'he works' does not require immediate capability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وإن ترك ولداً ولد في كتابته ولا وفاء سعى كأبيه على نجومه فإن أدى حكم بعتقه وعتق أبيه قبل موته وظاهر إطلاق المتن أنه لا فرق بين ما إذا ولد في أمته أو أمة الغير، وظاهر العلة تقييده بالأول لأن الولد دخل في كتابته وكسبه له الأداء فيخلفه في وصار أداؤه كأداء أبيه فجعل كأنه ترك وفاء مع الولد. والظاهر من قوله «يسعى» أن الولد المولود فيها لا بد أن يكون قادراً على السعي وليس كذلك. قال في الكافي : لو كاتب أمته على أنه بالخيار ثلاثة أيام فولدت في مدة الخيار وماتت وبقي الولد يبقي خياره وعقد الكتابة عند الإمام والثاني وله أن يجيزها، وإذا أجاز يسعى الولد على نجوم الأم وإذا أدى عتقت الأم في آخر جزء من أجزاء حياته وعتق ولدها وهذا استحسان، وعند الثالث تبطل الكتابة ولا يصح إجازة المولى وهو القياس. وفي المحيط : ولو ترك أم ولده معها ولد لا تباع واستسعت في الكتابة على نجوم المكاتب وإن لم يكن معها ولد باعها عند الإمام لأن حرية أو الولد لأجل الولد فإذا لم يكن ولد تباع. وعندهما لا تباع وتؤدي بدل الكتابة بعد موت المكاتب كما لو كان معها ولد. ولو حل على أولاده المولودين في الكتابة نجم ولم يؤدوا وبعضهم غائب لم يرد الحاضر في الرق حتى يرجع الغائب لأن الفسخ على الحاضر فسخ على الغائب وقد تعذر في حق الغائب فتعذر في حق الحاضر أيضاً. وفي الولوالجية وإذا مات المكاتب عن ولد مولود في الكتابة وولد مشتري معها فعندهما يسعيان في نجوم الأم فما اتصل في يد كل واحد منهما بعد موت الأم فهو له خاصة، وعند الإمام المولود يسعى على نجوم الأم ويؤدي بدل الكتابة وهو المطالب ويسعى الولد المشتري ويأخذ من كسبه ويؤجره بأمر القاضي، وما فضل يكون ميراثاً الأم فيكون بينهما. وفي الأصل الولد المولود في الكتابة يسعى في ديون الأب.
He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (And if he leaves a child born during his kitaba and no completion, he works like his father on his installments; if he pays, it is ruled that he is freed and his father is freed before his death. The apparent unqualified wording of the text is that there is no difference between whether the child was born in his own slave woman or the slave woman of another. The apparent cause restricts it to the first because the child entered into his kitaba and his earning is for the father's payment, so he succeeds him and his payment becomes like the father's payment, so it is as if he left sufficient funds with the child. And the apparent meaning of 'he works' is that the child born in it must be capable of working, but that is not so. It is said in al-Kafi: If he writes his slave woman with the option of three days, and she gives birth during the option period and dies, leaving the child, his option remains and the kitaba contract remains according to Imam and the Second (Abu Yusuf), and he may validate it. If he validates, the child works on the mother's installments; when he pays, the mother is freed in the last part of his life and her child is freed. This is istihsan. According to the Third (Muhammad al-Shaybani?), the kitaba is void and the master's validation is invalid; this is qiyas. And in al-Muhit: If he leaves his umm walad with a child, she is not sold and she is made to work on the mukatib's installments; if there is no child with her, she is sold according to Imam because her freedom is for the sake of the child; when there is no child, she is sold. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), she is not sold and she pays the kitaba after the mukatib's death, as if there were a child with her. And if an installment falls due on his children born in kitaba and they do not pay, and some are absent, the present one is not returned to slavery until the absent one returns because annulment against the present is annulment against the absent, and it is impossible regarding the absent, so it is impossible regarding the present as well. And in al-Walwalijiyya: If the mukatib dies leaving a child born in kitaba and a purchased child with her, according to them, both work on the mother's installments; whatever each earns after the mother's death is for him specifically. According to Imam, the born child works on the mother's installments and pays the kitaba, and he is the one required; the purchased child works and takes from his earnings, and he is hired by order of the judge; whatever remains is inheritance from the mother, so it is between them. And in al-Asl, the child born in kitaba works for the father's debts.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq, commented upon by the author. The core ruling: if a mukatib dies without completing his kitaba but leaves a child born during the kitaba, that child steps into the father's role. The child works and pays the installments, and upon payment, both the child and the father (posthumously) become free. The commentary clarifies that the text's apparent generality includes cases where the child was born in the father's own slave woman or another's, but the cause ('illa) suggests it only applies to the father's slave woman because the child is included in the kitaba. However, the ruling itself is broad. The author then discusses a case from al-Kafi: if a master contracts kitaba with a slave woman with a three-day option, and she gives birth and dies, the child remains under the contract according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Second), and the master can validate it; upon payment, mother and child are freed. This is istihsan. Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Third) says the contract is void, which is qiyas. Another case: if a mukatib dies leaving a umm walad (slave mother of his child) with a child, she is not sold but works on the kitaba; without a child, Imam says she is sold, while the two disciples say she is not sold. The passage also covers scenarios of absent children and the combination of a born child and a purchased child. The source al-Asl (by Muhammad al-Shaybani) confirms that the child born in kitaba works for the father's debts.

Key Terms
استحسان (istiḥsān): A method of juristic preference that overrides qiyas in certain cases for the sake of equity.
القياس (al-qiyās): Analogical reasoning; in this context, the strict analogy that the child cannot assume a contract he was not part of.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what happens to a child born during the father's kitaba when the father dies before completing it?
A) The child is sold to pay the kitaba
B) The child works on the installments and both become free upon payment
C) The kitaba is void and the child remains a slave
D) The child inherits the father's estate directly

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses istihsan to allow a child born during kitaba to assume the father's obligation, preserving the possibility of freedom despite the qiyas objection.

Purchased Child of a Mukatib: Immediate Payment or Installments?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on purchased child's kitaba obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions regarding a child purchased by a mukatib and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A purchased child is not automatically included in the kitaba contract; Imam demands immediate payment, Sahibayn allow installments.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a child purchased by a mukatib (a slave contracting for freedom). The matn states the ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa: the child must either pay the entire kitaba immediately or be returned to slavery. However, the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the child works on installments just like a child born during the kitaba. Understanding this difference requires analyzing the nature of the contract and the concept of saraya (extension of rulings). We will explore the reasoning, objections, and the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the Ruling in the Matn
Identify what the base text says: the purchased child must hasten the payment or be returned as a slave. Note that this is attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa.
The text says 'wa lahu qala' indicating Imam's view.
2
Compare the Sahibayn's Position
State that according to the two disciples, the purchased child follows the installments of the kitaba just like a child born in kitaba. Understand their basis: the child has taken the status of the mukatib's child.
3
Analyze Imam's Proof
Examine Imam's reasoning: the kitaba contract specifies a term (ajal) by condition, and the purchased child was not part of the original contract, so the term does not apply to him. The child must pay immediately or be returned.
Imam relies on the principle that the contract only binds those who entered it.
4
Address the Objection and Response
Review the objection from the earlier chapter (mukatib buying his father/son enters kitaba). Understand the rebuttal: 'entering kitaba' does not mean extension of the original kitaba but a new kitaba granted by the mukatib to his son. Immediate freedom is a special case due to necessity (like dying with sufficient funds).
The text distinguishes between true saraya and a separate grant.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
Identify which view is relied upon in later Hanafi fatwa. The Sahibayn's view is preferred because it promotes freedom and is more equitable.
Refer to al-Kafi and later works supporting the Sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولو ترك ولداً مشتري عجل البدل حالاً أو رد رقيقاً وظاهر إطلاق المتن أنه لا فرق في المشتري بين أن يكون ولد بعد الكتابة أو قبلها وسيأتي البيان، وهذا عند الإمام. وعندهما يسعى على نجومه كالمولود في الكتابة لأنه صار بمنزلته حتى جاز للمولى إعتاقه كما يجوز إعتاقه المكاتب بنفسه بخلاف سائر أكساب المكاتب فإنه لا يملك إعتاقه. وللإمام أن الأجل يثبت بالشرط في العقد فيثبت في حق من دخل تحت الكتابة والمشتري لم يدخل تحت العقد لأنه لم يضف إليه العقد ولم يسر حكمه إليه لكونه منفصلاً وقت الكتابة، وأورد في أول فصل المكاتب أن المكاتب إذا اشترى أباه أو ابنه دخل في كتابته، وأيضاً لو لم يسر حكمه إليه لما عتق عنده بأداء بدل الكتابة حالاً وأجيب أن المراد بدخول الولد المشتري في كتابه أبيه ليس السراية حكم عقد الكتابة الذي جرى بين المكاتب را ولاه إليه بل يجعل المكاتب مكاتباً لولده باشترائه اياه تحقيقاً للصلة وبأن عتق الولد المشتري عنده بأداء بدل الكتابة حالاً ليس لأجل السراية أيضاً بل لضرورة المكاتب إذا ذاك بمنزلة من مات عن وفاء، وقد أفصح عنه في الكافي حيث قال : وكان ينبغي أن يباع بعد موته لفوات المتبوع ولكن إذا عجل وأعطى من ساعته صار كأنه مات عن وفاء بخلاف المولود في الكتابة لأنه من مائه بعد الكتابة. قال رحمه الله : وإن اشترى ابنه فمات وترك وفاء ورثه ابنه لأنه لما أدى بدل الكتابة حكم بعتقه في آخر جزء من أجزاء حياته فيتبعه ولده في ذلك فيكونان حرين فظهر أنه مات حر عن ولد حر وقد بيناه قال رحمه الله: (وكذا لو كان هو وابنه مكاتبين كتابة واحدة لأنهما صارا كشخص واحد فإذا حكم بعتق أحدهما في وقت يعتق الآخر في ذلك الوقت ضرورة اتحاد العقد على ما بيناه فيصير حراً، مات عن ابن حر، ولو مات المكاتب وترك ثلاثة أولاد حر ومولود في الكتابة ومكاتب معه بعقد واحد ووصياً ترثه أولاد لما ذكرناه وبينا ويملك الوصي بيع العروض دون العقار والدراهم والدنانير لأن بيع العروض من باب الحفظ دون العقار والدراهم والدنانير. ولو مات الابن قبل أداء الكتابة لا يرثانه لأن أرثه ليس من حقوق كتابة أبيه فلا يظهر الاستيلاد حقه .
He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (And if he leaves a purchased child, he hastens the payment immediately or returns him as a slave. The apparent unqualified wording of the text is that there is no difference in the purchased child between whether he was born after the kitaba or before it, and the explanation will come. This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. According to them (the two disciples), he works on his installments like the child born in kitaba, because he has taken his status to the extent that the master may free him just as the mukatib may free himself, unlike other earnings of the mukatib, for he does not own their emancipation. For Imam, the term is established by condition in the contract, so it is established in favor of one who entered under the kitaba, and the purchased child did not enter under the contract because the contract was not extended to him and its ruling did not apply to him, as he was separate at the time of kitaba. It was objected that in the first chapter of the mukatib, if the mukatib buys his father or son, he enters into his kitaba. Also, if its ruling did not apply to him, he would not be freed by immediate payment of the kitaba. The answer is that by 'entering of the purchased child into his father's kitaba' is not meant the inclusion of the kitaba contract that was made between the mukatib and his master, but rather it makes the mukatib a grantor of kitaba to his son by purchasing him, to achieve connection. And the freedom of the purchased child by immediate payment of the kitaba is not due to inclusion either, but due to the necessity that the mukatib is in the position of one who died with sufficient funds. This is clarified in al-Kafi: He should have been sold after his death due to the loss of the followership, but if he hastens and pays immediately, it becomes as if he died with sufficient funds, unlike the child born in kitaba, because he is from his sperm after the kitaba. He (the author) said: If he buys his son and dies leaving sufficient funds, his son inherits him because when he paid the kitaba, it is ruled that he was freed in the last part of his life, so his son follows him in that, and both become free; thus it appears he died free leaving a free son. He (the author) said: Similarly, if he and his son are both mukatib in one kitaba, because they have become like one person; when it is ruled that one is freed at a time, the other is freed at that time due to the unity of the contract, as we explained. So he becomes free and dies leaving a free son. And if the mukatib dies leaving three children: a free child, a child born in kitaba, and a child who is mukatib with him in one contract, and an executor, the children inherit him due to what we mentioned and explained. The executor has the right to sell movable goods (uruud) but not real estate or dirhams and dinars, because selling movable goods is for preservation, unlike real estate and dirhams and dinars. And if the son dies before completing the kitaba, the two do not inherit him because his inheritance is not from the rights of his father's kitaba, so the cause of freedom does not appear in his right.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq deals with the situation of a mukatib who dies leaving a child he purchased (i.e., a slave he bought). The matn says the child must either pay the full kitaba immediately or be returned to slavery. This is Imam Abu Hanifa's position. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say the purchased child works on installments like a child born in kitaba, because he has taken the status of the mukatib's child to the extent that the master can free him. Imam's reasoning: the kitaba contract includes a term (ajal) set by condition; the purchased child was not part of the original contract, so the term does not apply to him; he must pay immediately. An objection is raised from the earlier chapter where a mukatib who buys his father or son includes them in his kitaba. The answer distinguishes: that inclusion is not via the original kitaba but by a new kitaba granted by the mukatib to his son. The freedom of the purchased child by immediate payment is a special case due to necessity, akin to dying with sufficient funds. The author then clarifies a related ruling: if a mukatib buys his own son and then dies with sufficient kitaba, the son inherits him because the father is freed at the last moment of life, and the son becomes free too, so the father dies free leaving a free son. Similarly, if both are co-mukatib in one kitaba, they are like one person, so they are freed together. Finally, the passage discusses a complex inheritance case with three children and an executor, stating the executor may sell movable goods but not real estate or coins, as selling movable goods is preservative.

Key Terms
ولد مشتري (walad mushtarā): A child who was purchased by the mukatib after the kitaba contract (as opposed to a child born in kitaba).
سراية (sarāya): The extension of a legal ruling from one party to another; here, the inclusion of the purchased child in the kitaba.
أجل (ajal): The term or period of the kitaba installments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position, what must a child purchased by a mukatib do if the mukatib dies before completing the kitaba?
A) Pay the entire kitaba immediately or be returned to slavery
B) Work on the installments of the kitaba like a child born in kitaba
C) Become free automatically because the mukatib died
D) Be sold to another master

Key Takeaway
The purchased child is not automatically part of the mukatib's kitaba; the Hanafi school prefers the Sahibayn's view allowing installments to facilitate freedom.
